Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Authority of the Four Imams in Hanafi Jurisprudence
Praise and authority-establishing preface

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the role of the four imams as described by al-Maydani and identify the purpose of his commentary on al-Quduri's al-Mukhtar.

Core Idea
The Hanafi madhhab, through its founding imams, is the authoritative framework for all legal rulings.

This passage is the introduction to a major Hanafi commentary. It establishes the foundational authority of the four great imams—especially Imam Abu Hanifa—and explains why the commentator undertook his work. Understanding this preface helps you place the entire commentary within the tradition of Hanafi scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of the introduction
Scan the Arabic text for the basmala, hamdalah, salawat, praise of the four imams, and the author's statement of intent. Each part serves a distinct purpose in establishing the work's legitimacy.
2
Analyze the praise of the four imams
The author says Allah placed them in the position of prophets among their people and commanded others to ask them. This elevates their authority in fiqh. Note that he specifically mentions 'the four famous imams' and then singles out Abu Hanifa as the 'Lamp of the Ummah'.
This is a standard trope in Hanafi introductions, asserting the school's primacy.
3
Connect the author's intent to the Hanafi school
The author states he was facilitated to work on a commentary of al-Quduri's al-Mukhtar, which is a foundational Hanafi matn. This demonstrates that the commentary aims to clarify and uphold Hanafi fiqh.
Al-Mukhtar is a concise manual; the commentary expands it while staying within Hanafi doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
المقدمة
الحمد الله رب العالمين، وأفضل الصلاة وأكمل التسليم على سيدنا محمد المبعوث رحمة للعالمين، وعلى آله وأصحابه أجمعين، وسائر السادة الفقهاء المجتهدين، والأئمة الأربعة المشهورين، من أقامَهُمُ اللهُ مَقامَ الأنبياء في أقوامهم، وأمَرَ سائر الناس بسؤالهم، والرجوع إلى أقوالهم، وأبقى ذكرهم ومذاهبهم، فعلى أقوالهـم مـدار الأحكام، وبمذاهبهم يُفتي فقهاء الإسلام. أئمة بهم يُقتدى، وإلى رأيهم يُنتَهى، تحيى القلوب بأخبارهم، وتحصل السعادة باقتفاء آثارهم. ورضي الله عن أتباعهم ومقلّديهم، ومن سار على دربهم وسَنَنِهم بإحسان إلى يوم الدين، وبعد: فإنه بنعمته وفضله سبحانه تتم الصالحات، وتقضى الحاجات، وتستجاب الدعوات، وتُحقق الأُمنيات الغاليات، وإنَّ ممَّا من به المولى الكريم سبحانه أن يسر لي العمل على كتاب: «اللباب في شرح الكتاب»، للعلامة الشيخ عبد الغني بن طالب الغنيمي الميداني الدمشقي، المولود سنة ۱۲۲۲هـ ، والمتوفى سنة ١٢٩٨هـ، رحمه الله تعالى، الذي شَرَحَ فيه: «المختصر في الفقه»، على مذهب سراج الأُمة أبي حنيفة النعمان، رَحِمَـه الـرحيم الرحمن، للإمام القدوري أبي
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The Introduction. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and the best of prayers and the most complete greetings be upon our master Muhammad, sent as a mercy to the worlds, and upon his family and all his companions, and all the master jurists who exercise ijtihad, and the four famous imams, whom Allah has placed in the position of prophets among their peoples, and commanded all people to ask them and refer to their statements, and perpetuated their mention and their schools—for upon their statements revolve rulings, and by their schools the jurists of Islam give fatwa. Imams who are followed, and their opinion is the final word; hearts are revived by their reports, and happiness is attained by following their footsteps. May Allah be pleased with their followers and emulators, and those who walk on their path and their way with excellence until the Day of Judgment. To proceed: Indeed, by His grace and bounty, the Exalted, righteous deeds are completed, needs are fulfilled, supplications are answered, and dear wishes are realized. And among what the Generous Lord, the Exalted, has bestowed upon me is that He facilitated for me the work on the book 'al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab' by the scholar Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani ibn Talib al-Ghanimi al-Maydani al-Dimashqi, born in 1222 AH and died in 1298 AH, may Allah have mercy on him, in which he explained 'al-Mukhtasar fi al-Fiqh' according to the school of the Lamp of the Ummah, Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man—may the Most Merciful, al-Rahman, have mercy on him—by Imam al-Quduri Abu
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the introduction (muqaddima) to the book 'al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab'. The author begins with the basmala, hamdalah, and salawat upon the Prophet, his family, and companions. He then praises the four famous imams of fiqh, emphasizing that they are the ones to whom people must turn for legal rulings, and that their statements and schools are the basis of Islamic jurisprudence. This establishes the authority of the Hanafi madhhab, which is the focus of this commentary. He specifically mentions Imam Abu Hanifa as the 'Lamp of the Ummah' (Siraj al-Umma). The author then explains that he has been facilitated by Allah to work on this commentary, which is a sharh of al-Quduri's 'al-Mukhtasar' (a foundational Hanafi fiqh text). He identifies the commentator as Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, providing his birth and death years. The tone is reverent and sets the stage for a work that aims to explain and uphold the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
المختصر في الفقه (al-Mukhtasar fi al-Fiqh): A concise legal manual by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH) summarizing Hanafi fiqh. It is a foundational matn in the school.
اللباب في شرح الكتاب (al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab): The title of the commentary being introduced, written by al-Maydani. 'al-Lubab' means 'the core' or 'the pith', indicating it extracts the essence of Sharh al-Kitab (which is a commentary on al-Hidayah or al-Quduri).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the introduction, why does the author emphasize the four famous imams?
A) To show that they are the only scholars of Islam
B) Because their statements are the basis of legal rulings and they are the ones people must refer to
C) To criticize other schools of thought
D) To highlight that they were prophets

Key Takeaway
The introduction establishes the four imams, especially Abu Hanifa, as the authoritative sources for fiqh, and the commentary aims to elucidate their school.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Introduction to al-Lubab and Its Authors
Opening preface of a commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key authors and texts that form the foundation of Hanafi fiqh education, and explain the historical significance of al-Lubab and Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri and its commentary al-Lubab are cornerstones of Hanafi legal education, relied upon for over a millennium.

This opening passage is not a legal ruling but a preface establishing the authority and lineage of the book you are about to study. It situates al-Lubab within the Hanafi tradition, naming its author al-Maydani and the original matn author al-Quduri. Understanding this context helps you appreciate why this text has been taught in madrasas for centuries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structure of the introduction
Notice the three parts: praise (hamd), salawat, and the author's statement of gratitude and purpose. This is a conventional opening that also serves to assert the text's orthodoxy.
2
Locate the key authors mentioned
Find the names of al-Quduri (author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri) and al-Maydani (author of al-Lubab). Note their birth and death years to understand their historical place.
Imam Abu Hanifa is also mentioned as the founder of the school.
3
Recognize the significance of the text
The passage states that al-Lubab is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and that it has been widely adopted in Hanafi circles. This signals the high authority of both texts.
4
Connect to the Hanafi curriculum
Understand that Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a foundational matn, and al-Lubab is a standard sharh. This explains why you are studying this work.
5
Reflect on the geographical spread
The author lists regions where al-Lubab is used: Levant, Hijaz, Turkey, Iraq, India, Pakistan, Egypt. This shows the global reach of the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
المقدمة
الحمد الله رب العالمين، وأفضل الصلاة وأكمل التسليم على سيدنا محمد المبعوث رحمة للعالمين، وعلى آله وأصحابه أجمعين، وسائر السادة الفقهاء المجتهدين، والأئمة الأربعة المشهورين، من أقامَهُمُ اللهُ مَقامَ الأنبياء في أقوامهم، وأمَرَ سائر الناس بسؤالهم، والرجوع إلى أقوالهم، وأبقى ذكرهم ومذاهبهم، فعلى أقوالهـم مـدار الأحكام، وبمذاهبهم يُفتي فقهاء الإسلام.
أئمة
بهم يُقتدى، وإلى رأيهم يُنتَهى، تحيى القلوب بأخبارهم،
وتحصل السعادة باقتفاء آثارهم.
ورضي الله عن أتباعهم ومقلّديهم، ومن سار على دربهم وسَنَنِهم بإحسان إلى يوم الدين، وبعد:
فإنه بنعمته وفضله سبحانه تتم الصالحات، وتقضى الحاجات، وتستجاب الدعوات، وتُحقق الأُمنيات الغاليات، وإنَّ ممَّا من به المولى الكريم سبحانه أن يسر لي العمل على كتاب: «اللباب في شرح الكتاب»، للعلامة الشيخ عبد الغني بن طالب الغنيمي الميداني الدمشقي، المولود سنة ۱۲۲۲هـ ، والمتوفى سنة ١٢٩٨هـ، رحمه الله تعالى، الذي شَرَحَ فيه: «المختصر في الفقه»، على مذهب سراج الأُمة أبي حنيفة النعمان، رَحِمَـه الـرحيم الرحمن، للإمام القدوري أبي
الحسين أحمد بن محمد البغدادي المولود سنة ٣٦٢ هـ، سنة ٤٢٨ هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
والمتوفى
وهكذا أعانني المولى جل وعلا على خدمة كل من كتاب اللباب، وأصله مختصر القدوري، والقيام على تحقيقهما، والعناية
بهما من وجوه متعددة، بحسب الجهد والطاقة.
-
وإن من تمام سعادتي اليوم أن أقدم ـ بتوفيق الله ـــ بـيـن أيــدي القراء الكرام هذه التحفة الحنفيةَ السَّنيَّة، والغنيمة الميدانية الدمشقية، منورة بخدمةٍ مَدَنيَّة، مُشرِقةً بحُلَّةٍ فَشِيبة بهيَّةٍ، فليذكرني الواقف عليها بصالح الدعاء، ورفع البلاء عن المسلمين في كافة الأرجاء. ولقد مضى على الطبعة الأولى لكتاب اللباب للميداني ـ والتي كانت في زمن مؤلّفه ـ أكثر من مائة وخمسين عاماً، حيث كانت في دار السلطنة العثمانية باسطنبول، سنة ١٢٧٥هـ، ثم تتابعت طبعات الكتاب، وكتب الله له القبول العظيم، كما كتب لأصله مختصر القدوري، وأصبح في الدروس بهجة للنفوس.
وهكذا تداول علماء الحنفية وطلاب المذهب الحنفي كتاب اللباب شرح مختصر القدوري، واعتمدوه كـل الاعتماد، وأصبح اللباب الكتاب المقرر المعتمد في المدارس والمعاهد وحلقات العلم، في بلاد الشام خاصة، وفي أنحاء كثيرة من البلاد: في الحجاز وتركيا والعراق والهند وباكستان وغيرها من المواضع. وذلك _ بعد تقدير الله وفضله بسبب المكانة العظمى لمختصر القدوري في المذهب، وكذلك ما لكتاب اللباب من المزايا العلمية
ومصر
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The Introduction. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and the best of prayers and complete peace be upon our master Muhammad, sent as a mercy to the worlds, and upon his family and all his Companions, and all the noble jurists who strive, and the four famous imams, whom Allah established in the position of prophets among their peoples, and commanded all people to ask them and refer to their statements, and He preserved their memory and schools; upon their statements revolve the rulings, and by their schools the jurists of Islam issue fatwas. Imams by whom one follows, and to whose opinion one resorts; hearts are revived by their reports, and happiness is attained by following their traces. May Allah be pleased with their followers and imitators, and those who walk on their path and sunnah with excellence until the Day of Judgment. After: indeed by His grace and favor, may He be glorified, good deeds are completed, needs are fulfilled, supplications are answered, and precious wishes are realized. Among what the noble Lord has bestowed upon me is that He facilitated for me to work on the book: 'al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab' by the scholar Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani ibn Talib al-Ghanimi al-Maydani al-Dimashqi, born 1222 AH, died 1298 AH, may Allah have mercy on him, who explained in it: 'al-Mukhtasar fi al-Fiqh' according to the school of the Lamp of the Ummah, Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man, may the Most Merciful have mercy on him, by Imam al-Quduri Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Baghdadi, born 362 AH, died 428 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. Thus Allah helped me to serve both the book al-Lubab and its original Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and to edit them and care for them in multiple ways according to effort and ability. And it is part of my complete happiness today that I present, by the grace of Allah, to the noble readers this lofty Hanafi masterpiece and the Maydani Damascene treasure, illuminated by a Medinian service, shining with a beautiful new garment. May the one who comes across it remember me with righteous supplication and the removal of affliction from the Muslims in all regions. More than one hundred and fifty years have passed since the first edition of al-Lubab by al-Maydani, which was during the time of its author, in the Ottoman Sultanate in Istanbul, in the year 1275 AH. Then editions followed one after another, and Allah wrote for it great acceptance, as He wrote for its original Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and it became in lessons a delight for souls. Thus the Hanafi scholars and students of the Hanafi school passed around the book al-Lubab, the commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and fully relied upon it. Al-Lubab became the approved prescribed book in schools, institutes, and circles of knowledge, especially in the Levant, and in many regions: in Hijaz, Turkey, Iraq, India, Pakistan, and other places. That, after the decree of Allah and His grace, due to the great status of Mukhtasar al-Quduri in the school, and also due to the scientific merits of the book al-Lubab, and Egypt.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is the opening front matter of al-Lubab, a commentary (sharh) on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author begins with the basmalah and praise of Allah, followed by salawat on the Prophet and his Companions. He extols the four famous imams of fiqh, emphasizing that their statements are the basis for rulings and fatwas. He then states that by Allah's grace he was able to work on this commentary. He introduces the author of the original text, al-Quduri (Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Baghdadi, 362-428 AH), and the commentator, 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (1222-1298 AH). He describes his effort to serve both the commentary and its original. He mentions the first edition in Istanbul (1275 AH) and the widespread acceptance of al-Lubab in Hanafi circles, especially in the Levant, Hijaz, Turkey, Iraq, India, Pakistan, and Egypt. The passage establishes the significance and authority of the text within the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): The title of the commentary, meaning 'the core' or 'the essence', authored by 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise Hanafi fiqh text by Abu al-Husayn Ahmad al-Quduri (362-428 AH), serving as the base matn for al-Lubab.
المذهب الحنفي (al-madhhab al-Hanafi): The school of jurisprudence attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who is the author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri?
A) 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
B) Abu al-Husayn Ahmad al-Quduri
C) Imam Abu Hanifa
D) Sultan of the Ottoman Empire

Key Takeaway
Al-Lubab is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and both texts have been central to Hanafi education for centuries, with al-Lubab adopted widely across the Islamic world.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Understanding the Editor's Preface: The Importance of Tahqeeq in Hanafi Texts
Editor's preface detailing errors in earlier prints and his methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key editorial problems in previous editions of Al-Lubab and explain why textual accuracy is critical for deriving correct fiqh rulings.

Core Idea
A corrupted text can change the hukm — tahqeeq safeguards the madhhab's transmitted rulings.

This passage is the editor's preface to the new critical edition of Al-Lubab. It reveals that earlier prints suffered from distortions (tahrif) and omissions (isqat), sometimes altering the fiqh ruling itself. As students of the Hanafi school, understanding the editorial process helps us appreciate the reliability of the text we study and avoid perpetuating errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problems
List the two major defects: tahrif (distortion of words) and isqat (omissions), as well as the poor layout (cramped, unparagraphed) that caused overlapping issues.
These defects are explicitly stated in the introduction.
2
Understand the consequences
Recognize that a distorted word can change the fiqh ruling (e.g., altering a condition or obligation). Omissions can lose entire rulings.
The editor gives an example: 'sometimes changes the fiqh ruling in the issue.'
3
Appreciate the solution
See the editor's multi-volume structure: one volume of study, four volumes of Al-Lubab with Mukhtasar Al-Quduri in the margins, and a separate volume of Mukhtasar alone. This ensures accuracy and ease of access.
The goal is to 'establish a correct text' and 'facilitate access to the desired.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقدمة

الكثيرة، مما سيأتي بيانه بالتفصيل، كل ذلك جعل اللباب هكذا سائداً شائعاً متداولاً معتمداً.
وشاء الله تعالى لكتاب اللباب في هذه السنين الماضية الطويلة أن ينتشر بين طلاب العلم بدون تحقيق لنصوصه، وتحرير لألفاظه، ولم يُعط حقه أبداً من العناية الواجبة له.
وحَصَل بسبب ذلك ما حصل في طبعاته السابقة من الخلل الكبير في جوانب متعددة، مما يُتعجب منه كلَّ العَجَب، من أهمها تحريف لكلمات كثيرة في نصه، مما يُغيّر الحكم الفقهي في المسألة أحياناً، مع وجود أسقاط كثيرة من نصه، حتى بلغ بعضها جملة كاملة، أو سطراً أو سطرين، بل أكثر من ذلك في مواضع عديدة.
كل هذا جعل في نص طبعات اللباب إشكالات كثيرة تجعل القارىء المتفقة يقف متحيّراً مضطرباً، لا يجد لها حلاً، وتُسبب فهماً خاطئاً لمسائل كثيرة في الكتاب.
هذا، مع عدم إشراق طبعاته السابقة، ومجيئ النص فيها مزحوماً مرصوصاً غير مفقر، مما سبب تداخل المسائل بعضها في بعض.
كما تفقد تلك الطبعات ما تمس إليه حاجة القراء، من شرح عبارات كثيرة غامضة، وبيان معنى ضمائر في كثير من الألفاظ غـيـر واضحة، ونحو هذا من التحقيقات العلمية الواجبة.
ولقد سعدت أيَّما سعادة في هذه الرحلة العلميـة الطيبـة المباركة في خدمة اللباب وأصله مختصر القدوري، والتي دامــت ســت سنوات، والله الحمد، وسأذكر بالتفصيل بعد قليل إن شاء الله بيان عملي في تحقيقهما، والخدمات العلمية المهمة التي قمـت بهـا مـن وجوه كثيرة، والمنهج الذي سرت عليه في ذلك.
والمقصود من عملي هذا السعي لإثبات نص صحيح لهما، مع تيسير الوصول إلى المطلوب على الطالبين وتقريب الكتاب إلى أفهام المقتبسين.
وقد قدَّمتُ على نص اللباب دراسة موسعة عن اللباب ومختصر القدوري، جاءت في مقدمة، وتمهيد، وبابين كبيرين : الباب الأول: دراسة عن العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، وكتابه اللباب، وفيه عدة فصول، وفي كل فصل عدة مباحث. الباب الثاني : دراسة عن الإمام القدوري، ومختصره، وفيـه عـدة فصول، وفي كل منها عدة مباحث، ومنها فـصـل طـويـل عـن شـروح القدوري والأعمال العلمية التي قامت عليه، وقد بلغت ١٢٢ عملاً. وجاء في خاتمة ذلك فهرس المصادر الدراسة والتحقيق، ثم فهرس آخر لموضوعات هذا المجلد.
وهكذا جعلت هذه الدراسة في مجلد واحد، ثم تلاه اللباب للعلامة الميداني في أربع مجلدات وفي أعلى صفحاته مختصر القدوري موزعاً على الشرح ، ثم جاء مجلد سادس خــاص فـيـه نـص مختصر القدوري، مفرداً بدون أي تعليق؛ ليكون متتابعاً متتالياً كما أراد مؤلفه رحمه الله تعالى.
هذا، وقد كانت صلتي باللباب قبل هذا قديمة، فقد أكرمني
The Introduction

... many, which will be explained in detail later, all of that made Al-Lubab thus prevalent, widespread, circulated, and authoritative.
And Allah Almighty willed that the book Al-Lubab in these long past years should spread among students of knowledge without verification of its texts and editing of its expressions, and it was never given its due care.
And because of that, what happened in its previous editions of great defect in various aspects occurred, which is astonishing indeed. The most important of these is the distortion of many words in its text, which sometimes changes the fiqh ruling in the issue, along with many omissions from its text, to the extent that some of them reached a complete sentence, or a line or two, even more than that in many places.
All this caused in the text of the editions of Al-Lubab many problems that make the knowledgeable reader stand bewildered and disturbed, finding no solution for them, and cause a wrong understanding of many issues in the book.
This, in addition to the lack of clarity of its previous editions, and the text coming in them congested, packed, and unparagraphed, which caused the overlapping of issues with each other.
Likewise, those editions lack what readers need, such as explanation of many obscure expressions, clarification of the meaning of pronouns in many unclear words, and similar necessary scholarly verifications.
And I was extremely delighted in this blessed and good scholarly journey in serving Al-Lubab and its original Mukhtasar Al-Quduri, which lasted six years, and praise be to Allah. I will mention in detail shortly, Allah willing, the explanation of my work in verifying them, and the important scholarly services I performed from many aspects, and the methodology I followed in that.
And the purpose of my work is to strive to establish a correct text for both, while facilitating access to the desired for students and making the book closer to the understanding of seekers.
And I have presented before the text of Al-Lubab an extensive study about Al-Lubab and Mukhtasar Al-Quduri, which came in an introduction, a preamble, and two large chapters: the first chapter: a study about the scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani Al-Maydani and his book Al-Lubab, containing several sections, each section containing several topics. The second chapter: a study about Imam Al-Quduri and his Mukhtasar, containing several sections, each containing several topics, including a long section about the commentaries of Al-Quduri and the scholarly works that were done on it, which reached 122 works. And at the end of that, an index of sources for the study and verification, then another index of the topics of this volume.
Thus I made this study in one volume, then followed by Al-Lubab of the scholar Al-Maydani in four volumes, and at the top of its pages is Mukhtasar Al-Quduri distributed over the commentary, then a sixth volume specialized in the text of Mukhtasar Al-Quduri alone without any commentary, so that it is consecutive and continuous as its author intended, may Allah have mercy on him.
And this, my connection with Al-Lubab before this was old; indeed, He honored me...
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is the editor's preface (front matter). It begins by lamenting the poor state of previous editions of Al-Lubab, which were printed without proper scholarly editing (tahqeeq). The editor identifies two major defects: (1) tahrif (distortion of words) that sometimes changes the legal ruling, and (2) isqat (omissions) ranging from phrases to entire sentences. Additionally, the layout was cramped and unparagraphed, causing overlap between different legal issues. The editor then outlines his six-year project to produce a correct edition, including an extensive study in one volume, the main text of Al-Lubab in four volumes with Mukhtasar Al-Quduri in the margins, and a separate volume containing only the Mukhtasar. The tone is apologetic and aspirational, aiming to serve students by providing an accurate text and clear commentary. This is not a fiqh ruling but rather a scholarly apparatus describing the methodology of the edition.

Key Terms
اللباب (Al-Lubab): The title of the commentary by Abdul Ghani Al-Maydani on Mukhtasar Al-Quduri. Literally 'the core' or 'the essence'.
تحقيق (tahqeeq): Scholarly critical editing of a text, involving verification of the manuscript, correction of errors, and addition of explanatory notes.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar Al-Quduri): The foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad Al-Quduri (d. 428 AH). It is a concise summary of Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the editor, which of the following was NOT mentioned as a problem in previous editions of Al-Lubab?
A) Distortion of words (tahrif)
B) Omissions of sentences (isqat)
C) Incorrect attribution of authorship
D) Cramped and unparagraphed layout

Key Takeaway
The accuracy of a fiqh text directly impacts the validity of legal rulings derived from it; tahqeeq is essential for preserving the integrity of the madhhab.

Introduction and Front Matter

Understanding the Editor's Introduction: Structure and Significance of Al-Lubab Edition
Editor's introduction to a critical edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the structure of Sa'id Bakdash's critical edition of Al-Lubab and identify the scholarly significance of the editor's study and personal ijazah chain.

Core Idea
A critical edition's value lies in its apparatus: the editor's study, manuscript work, and scholarly lineage.

This lesson examines the editor's introduction to the critical edition of Al-Lubab. You will learn how the edition is organized, what scholarly work the editor performed, and why his personal connection to the text through teachers and ijazah matters for the reliability of the text. This understanding is essential for using any critical edition of a classical Hanafi fiqh work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose and scope of the edition
The editor states he aims to establish a correct text for both Al-Lubab and Mukhtasar al-Quduri, facilitating access for students. Note the emphasis on textual accuracy and pedagogical utility.
This is a typical goal for a critical edition in Islamic scholarship.
2
Analyze the volume structure
The edition is in six volumes: one volume of introductory study, four volumes of Al-Lubab (with Mukhtasar al-Quduri at the top of each page), and a sixth volume containing only the matn of Mukhtasar al-Quduri without commentary.
The separate matn volume allows continuous reading as intended by al-Quduri.
3
Recognize the editor's scholarly credentials
The editor shares his study of Al-Lubab under Shaykh Abd al-Ghaffar al-Darubi al-Himsi, from whom he received an ijazah, and acknowledges the encouragement of Shaykh Wasfi al-Himsi. This establishes his transmission chain and authority.
Ijazah is a traditional method of authorizing transmission of knowledge in Islam.

والمقصود من عملي هذا السعي لإثبات نص صحيح لهما، مع تيسير الوصول إلى المطلوب على الطالبين وتقريب الكتاب إلى أفهام المقتبسين.

وهكذا جعلت هذه الدراسة في مجلد واحد، ثم تلاه اللباب للعلامة الميداني في أربع مجلدات وفي أعلى صفحاته مختصر القدوري موزعاً على الشرح ، ثم جاء مجلد سادس خــاص فـيـه نـص مختصر القدوري، مفرداً بدون أي تعليق؛ ليكون متتابعاً متتالياً كما أراد مؤلفه رحمه الله تعالى.
هذا، وقد كانت صلتي باللباب قبل هذا قديمة، فقد أكرمني

المقدمة
۹
الله تعالى بقراءته قراءةَ دَرس على شيخنا العلامة المقرىء الفقيه الحنفي المُتَّقِنِ سيدي فضيلة الشيخ عبد الغفار ابن الشيخ عبد الفتـاح الــدروبي الحمصي، رحمه الله تعالى، وأعلى مقامه في عليين، المولود سنة ١٣٣٨هـ، والمتوفى في جدة في التاسع عشر من شهر محرم الحرام، سنة ١٤٣٠هـ ، المدفون في مقبرة المعلاة بمكة المكرمة.
فقد قرأته عليه مع مجموعة من الإخوة الكرام من طلاب العلم بمكة المكرمة أيام دراستي في جامعة أم القرى، بدءاً من سنة ١٤٠٦هـ، إلى أن يسر الله ختم قراءته في منتصف عام ١٤١٤هـ، وقد أجازني به الشيخ رحمه الله إجازة خاصة، ولله الحمد.
وألمعُ هنا إلى أنه كان لشيخنا العلامة الفقيه الحنفي المتقن، الواعظ بحاله ومقاله سيدي فضيلة الشيخ وصفي بن أحمد مسدي الحمصي، المولود سنة ١٣٣٥هـ، المقيم في مدينة جدة، حفظه الله تعالى، وأمتع المسلمين به بخير وعافية، أنه كان له الأثر الكبير في دفعي وتنشيطي لخدمة اللباب، وحتي على التعجيل في تحقيقـه وإخراجه، وكان حفظه الله كلما قابلته سألني عنه، وعن موعد انتهاء خدمته، وطبعه ونشره، وكان لدعواته الصالحة التي ما زال يُكرمني ويخصني بها الأثر الواضح، جزاه الله عني خير الجزاء،
وأقر الله عينه بكل ما يرجوه ويصبو إليه من خير الدنيا والآخرة. والشكر موصول لجميع مشايخي وأساتذتي أصحاب الفـضـل والفضيلة، وأهل الجود بالإفادات والإرشادات، وكذلك لكل الإخوة الكرام ممن كانت له يد مساعدة في خدمة هذا الكتاب المبارك.
The Introduction. My work in editing them, and the important scholarly services that I have undertaken from many aspects, and the methodology I have followed in that. And the purpose of my work is to strive to establish a correct text for both, while facilitating access to what is sought for students and bringing the book closer to the understanding of learners. 6 And I have prefaced the text of Al-Lubab with an extensive study about Al-Lubab and Mukhtasar Al-Quduri, which came in an introduction, a preface, and two major chapters: The first chapter: a study of the scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani and his book Al-Lubab, containing several sections, each with several discussions. The second chapter: a study of Imam al-Quduri and his Mukhtasar, containing several sections, each with several discussions, including a long section on the commentaries of Al-Quduri and the scholarly works based upon it, which reached 122 works. And at the conclusion of that, an index of sources for study and verification, then another index of topics for this volume. Thus I made this study in one volume, then followed by Al-Lubab of Sheikh al-Maydani in four volumes, and at the top of its pages, Mukhtasar al-Quduri distributed over the commentary, then came a sixth volume specifically containing the text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri alone without any commentary, so that it may be continuous and sequential as its author, may Allah have mercy on him, intended. And this, my connection with Al-Lubab before this was old, for Allah honored me by reading it as a lesson under our teacher, the distinguished scholar, reciter, Hanafi jurist, proficient, my master, honourable Sheikh Abd al-Ghaffar ibn Sheikh Abd al-Fattah al-Darubi al-Himsi, may Allah have mercy on him, and elevate his station in the highest ranks, born in 1338 AH, died in Jeddah on the 19th of Muharram al-Haram, 1430 AH, buried in al-Ma'alah cemetery in Makkah al-Mukarramah. I read it with a group of noble brothers from students of knowledge in Makkah during my studies at Umm al-Qura University, starting from 1406 AH until Allah facilitated its completion in mid-1414 AH, and the Sheikh gave me a special permission (ijazah) for it, praise be to Allah. I also mention here that our teacher, the distinguished Hanafi jurist, proficient, preacher by his state and speech, my master, honourable Sheikh Wasfi ibn Ahmad Masdi al-Himsi, born 1335 AH, resident in Jeddah, may Allah preserve him and benefit Muslims through him with goodness and health, had a great impact in motivating and encouraging me to serve Al-Lubab, even to hasten in its edition and publication, and whenever I met him, he would ask me about it and about the time of finishing its service, printing, and publication. His righteous supplications, with which he continues to honour me, had a clear effect. May Allah reward him well on my behalf, and may Allah comfort his eyes with all the goodness of this world and the Hereafter that he hopes and aspires to. Gratitude is also extended to all my teachers and professors, the virtuous and learned, and those generous with benefit and guidance, as well as to all noble brothers who had a helping hand in serving this blessed book.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction, which is a front-matter section typical of academic critical editions. The editor, Sa'id Bakdash, outlines his methodology for producing a reliable text of two classical Hanafi works: 'Al-Lubab' by Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (a commentary on 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri') and 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' itself. He explains that he has arranged the edition in six volumes: one volume of introductory study, four volumes of 'Al-Lubab' with the matn of 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' printed at the top of each page, and a final standalone volume containing only the matn of 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' without commentary. The editor then shares his personal history of studying 'Al-Lubab' with his teacher Sheikh Abd al-Ghaffar al-Darubi al-Himsi in Makkah, receiving an ijazah (permission to teach) for the book. He also credits another teacher, Sheikh Wasfi al-Himsi, for encouraging him to undertake the project. This biographical information establishes the editor's credentials and the scholarly lineage of the edition, which is important for students to trust the reliability of the text. The passage does not contain any legal rulings or fiqh discussions.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), summarising the rulings of the school.
اللباب (Al-Lubab): A commentary (sharh) on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (d. 1298 AH), extracting the core rulings.
التحقيق (Al-Tahqiq): Critical editing of a classical manuscript to produce a reliable text.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Humility of Scholars: Ijaza and the Imperfection of Human Works in Hanafi Tradition
Biographical introduction and scholarly humility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the role of ijaza in Hanafi scholarship and analyze the principle that only the Quran is free from error.

Core Idea
No human book is perfect; only the Quran is free from error — a Hanafi principle of scholarly humility.

The author's introduction is more than a routine acknowledgement. It reveals two key aspects of Hanafi scholarly culture: the transmission of knowledge through formal permission (ijaza) and the humble recognition that all human works are fallible. This lesson unpacks these concepts, showing how they shape the way Hanafi fiqh is studied and transmitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key figures
List the author, his two teachers (Abd al-Ghaffar al-Darubi and Wasfi al-Himsi), and the scholar quoted (Alauddin al-Bukhari). Note their roles.
The author is a Hanafi scholar writing a commentary on al-Quduri's matn.
2
Understand ijaza
The author received a 'special ijaza' from his first teacher. Define ijaza as a formal permission to transmit and teach the book, signifying mastery.
In Hanafi tradition, ijaza is a rigorous certification, not a mere formality.
3
Analyze al-Bukhari's quote
Read the quote: al-Bukhari admits that despite his best efforts, errors will occur. Identify the two types of errors mentioned (khatal and khata).
Al-Bukhari cites al-Muzani and al-Shafi'i to reinforce that only Allah's book is errorless.
4
Connect to Islamic theology
The belief that only the Quran is free from error (isma) is foundational. This humility extends to all human scholarship, including fiqh works.
This does not undermine the authority of Hanafi fiqh; it invites respectful critique within the tradition.
5
Apply to student mindset
Reflect: How should a student approach Hanafi texts? With respect, but also with awareness that they are human efforts requiring study and verification.
The author's request for corrections shows the collaborative nature of knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقدمة
الله تعالى بقراءته قراءةَ دَرس على شيخنا العلامة المقرىء الفقيه الحنفي المُتَّقِنِ سيدي فضيلة الشيخ عبد الغفار ابن الشيخ عبد الفتـاح الــدروبي الحمصي، رحمه الله تعالى، وأعلى مقامه في عليين، المولود سنة ١٣٣٨هـ، والمتوفى في جدة في التاسع عشر من شهر محرم الحرام، سنة ١٤٣٠هـ ، المدفون في مقبرة المعلاة بمكة المكرمة.
فقد قرأته عليه مع مجموعة من الإخوة الكرام من طلاب العلم بمكة المكرمة أيام دراستي في جامعة أم القرى، بدءاً من سنة ١٤٠٦هـ، إلى أن يسر الله ختم قراءته في منتصف عام ١٤١٤هـ، وقد أجازني به الشيخ رحمه الله إجازة خاصة، ولله الحمد.
وألمعُ هنا إلى أنه كان لشيخنا العلامة الفقيه الحنفي المتقن، الواعظ بحاله ومقاله سيدي فضيلة الشيخ وصفي بن أحمد مسدي الحمصي، المولود سنة ١٣٣٥هـ، المقيم في مدينة جدة، حفظه الله تعالى، وأمتع المسلمين به بخير وعافية، أنه كان له الأثر الكبير في دفعي وتنشيطي لخدمة اللباب، وحتي على التعجيل في تحقيقـه وإخراجه، وكان حفظه الله كلما قابلته سألني عنه، وعن موعد انتهاء خدمته، وطبعه ونشره، وكان لدعواته الصالحة التي ما زال يُكرمني ويخصني بها الأثر الواضح، جزاه الله عني خير الجزاء،
وأقر الله عينه بكل ما يرجوه ويصبو إليه من خير الدنيا والآخرة. والشكر موصول لجميع مشايخي وأساتذتي أصحاب الفـضـل والفضيلة، وأهل الجود بالإفادات والإرشادات، وكذلك لكل الإخوة الكرام ممن كانت له يد مساعدة في خدمة هذا الكتاب المبارك.

وفي ختام هذه المقدمة أتمثَّل بما قاله الإمام الفقيه الأصولي الحنفي علاء الدين البخاري، المتوفى سنة ٧٣٠هـ، في مقدمة شرحه على أصول الإمام البزدوي علي بن محمد، المتوفى سنة ٤٨٢هـ، رحمهما الله تعالى المسمى : كشف الأسرار ) ، حيث قال:
(1)
وإني وإن لم آلُ جهداً في خدمة هذا الكتاب وترتيبه، ولم أدخــر جداً في تسديده وتهذيبه، فلا بد من أن يقع فيه عَشْرَةٌ وزَكل، وأن يوجد فيه خطأً وخَطَل (۲) ، فلا يتعجب الواقف عليـه منـه، فإن ذلك مما لا ينجو منه أحد، ولا يَستنكفُه بَشَرٌ.
وقد قال المزني: قرأتُ كتاب «الرسالة» على الشافعي ثمانين مرةً، فما من مرَّةٍ إلا وكان يقف على خطأ، فقال الشافعي: هيه! ـ أي حسبك - أبى الله أن يكون كتاب صحيحاً غير كتابه.
فالمأمول ممن وقف عليه بعد أن جانب التعصب والتعسف ، ونَبَذَ وراء ظهره التكلُّف والتصلُّف، أن يسعى في إصلاحه بقدر الوسـع والإمكان، أداء لحقِّ الأُخوة في الإيمان، وإحرازاً لحسن الأُحدوثة بين الأنام، وادخاراً لجزيل المثوبة في دار السلام، والله الموفق والمثيب، عليه أتوكل وإليه أنيب». اهـ
هذا، وأسأل الله تعالى به وبكرمه وبرحمته الخاصة أن يجعل عملي هذا خالصاً لوجهه الكريم، وأن يكتب به النفع، وأن يجعله في
The Introduction: Allah Almighty, by reading it as a lesson reading upon our teacher, the distinguished, the reciter, the jurist, the Hanafi, the precise, my master, his excellency Sheikh Abd al-Ghaffar ibn Sheikh Abd al-Fattah al-Darubi al-Himsi, may Allah have mercy on him and elevate his station in the highest, born in 1338 AH, died in Jeddah on the 19th of Muharram al-Haram, 1430 AH, buried in the Ma'la cemetery in Mecca. I read it upon him with a group of honorable brothers from the students of knowledge in Mecca during my studies at Umm al-Qura University, starting from 1406 AH until Allah facilitated completing its reading in mid-1414 AH, and the Sheikh, may Allah have mercy on him, granted me a special ijaza (permission), praise be to Allah. I mention here that our teacher, the distinguished Hanafi jurist, the preacher by his state and speech, my master, his excellency Sheikh Wasfi ibn Ahmad Masdi al-Himsi, born 1335 AH, residing in Jeddah, may Allah protect him, had a great impact in motivating me to serve al-Lubab, even hastening its verification and publication. Every time I met him, he asked me about it, and about the completion of its service, printing, and publication, and his righteous supplications had clear effect. May Allah reward him. I also thank all my teachers and brothers who helped in serving this blessed book. At the end of this introduction, I quote Imam al-Faqih al-Usuli al-Hanafi Alauddin al-Bukhari, d. 730 AH, from his commentary on Usul al-Bazdawi (Kashf al-Asrar): 'I have spared no effort in serving this book and arranging it, yet errors and mistakes will inevitably occur. Let no one be surprised, for no one is immune. Al-Muzani said: I read al-Risalah to al-Shafi'i eighty times, and each time he found an error. Al-Shafi'i said: enough! Allah refused that any book be perfect except His Book.' So I ask that whoever finds errors correct them. I ask Allah to accept this work.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is from the introduction (muqaddimah) of the author, a Hanafi scholar who wrote a commentary (sharh) on al-Quduri's matn. He begins by acknowledging his teacher, Sheikh Abd al-Ghaffar al-Darubi al-Himsi, under whom he studied the book, and notes that he received a special ijaza (permission to teach) from him. He also acknowledges another teacher, Sheikh Wasfi al-Himsi, who motivated him to publish this work. The author then quotes a well-known passage from Imam Alauddin al-Bukhari's Kashf al-Asrar, a commentary on al-Bazdawi's Usul. In that quote, al-Bukhari humbly states that despite his best efforts, errors will still appear in his work, and no human book is free of mistakes. He cites an anecdote about al-Muzani and al-Shafi'i to illustrate that even great scholars recognized this. The author then asks readers to correct any errors they find, hoping for divine reward. This introduction serves as a preface, setting the tone of humility and scholarly rigor.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijaza): A permission or license from a teacher to transmit or teach a specific book or body of knowledge.
الخطأ (al-khata): Error or mistake, as opposed to deliberate falsehood.
الخطل (al-khatal): Grave or serious error, as defined in the editor's footnote.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main purpose of the quotation from Alauddin al-Bukhari in this introduction?
A) To show the author's extensive knowledge of usul al-fiqh
B) To acknowledge that despite careful work, human errors are inevitable in any book
C) To criticize readers who find faults in scholarly works
D) To establish the superiority of al-Bukhari's commentary over others

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi tradition, scholarly works are humbly presented as human efforts, and the chain of transmission (ijaza) ensures their connection to the original authors.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Understanding Critical Editions in Hanafi Fiqh
Editorial introduction describing the critical edition process and methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the importance of critical editions in preserving the Hanafi textual tradition and identify the editor's methodology for establishing a reliable text.

Core Idea
A reliable text is the foundation of sound fiqh—critical editions protect the author's intended rulings.

Before studying any fiqh ruling, one must ensure the text itself is authentic. Manuscripts can contain errors, omissions, or additions. This preface introduces the meticulous work of a modern editor who compares multiple manuscript copies to restore the original text of two seminal Hanafi works: Mukhtasar al-Quduri and its commentary al-Lubab. Understanding this process helps us appreciate the care required in transmitting sacred knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the Need for Textual Criticism
Understand that hand-copied manuscripts can vary due to scribal mistakes, deliberate changes, or regional differences. The editor's goal is to identify and correct these to recover the author's original text.
2
Identify the Editor's Sources
The editor collected the oldest, most accurate, and most precious manuscripts of both Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Lubab, as well as other commentaries. This multi-source approach is standard in critical editions.
Note: Using multiple manuscripts allows cross-checking to spot errors.
3
Understand Types of Textual Variants
Variants can be in wording, expression, additions, deletions, or even additions of entire rulings or conditions. The editor only notes important variants in his footnotes.
Many variants are insignificant and are suppressed to keep the edition readable.
4
Appreciate the Editor's Judgement
The editor states he strived to establish the 'sound or more correct text' (النص السليم الصحيح أو الأصح). This involves scholarly judgement based on manuscript age, quality, and internal consistency.
The editor does not claim infallibility; he presents his best effort.

Introduction
11
A safeguard of acceptance, and in the path of His pleasure from me, and from those who seek refuge with me on the day of standing before Him and presenting [one's deeds].
(1)
6
And it is hoped from His bounty and generosity that He makes it a lasting legacy and a truthful tongue in later generations, and a good remembrance in this world, and a treasure in the Hereafter. He is the best to hope from, and the most generous to ask (2).
And I ask Him, Glorified and Exalted, to forgive us our sins and our excesses in our affairs, and to keep us firm on what pleases Him, with pardon, well-being, and perpetual good health in religion, world, and Hereafter, for us, our parents, our teachers, our families, everyone who has a right upon us, and for all Muslim men and women. He, Sublime, is the Generous One whom the hopes of the hopeful do not exceed, and the prayer of those who supplicate is not rejected before Him, and no servant who seeks his Lord fails.
6
And may Allah bless our Master Muhammad and all his family and Companions, and grant abundant peace, and all praise is for Allah first and last.
Written by
Prof. Dr. Sa'id bin Muhammad Yahya Bakdash

12
Preface
My work in serving al-Lubab and Mukhtasar al-Quduri and my methodology in editing
I have presented this in twenty-three paragraphs, which are: 1- I collected the oldest, most accurate, and most precious available manuscript copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, as well as collected manuscript and printed copies of al-Lubab from the time of the author and after. Likewise, by Allah's grace, I obtained the largest possible number of manuscript and printed commentaries of al-Quduri. After that, I strove to establish the sound or more correct text in both Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Lubab. 2- The textual variants in each of the two books are many, very many, for reasons to be explained, so I did not note them in my comments except what was important and needed to be indicated.
These variants, especially for the copies of al-Quduri, may be in differences in wording, expression, or in deletion or addition of a letter, word, sentence, or more, or in addition of a ruling, condition, or restriction, and so on, varying in importance. I have recorded what I deemed to be the text of al-Quduri, and what is sound or more correct from the text, and I have suppressed much...
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the critical edition's preface (تمهيد) written by the editor, Dr. Sa'id Bakdash. It begins with pious invocations and praises, then outlines his editorial methodology for the two texts: Mukhtasar al-Quduri (the base matn) and al-Lubab (its commentary by al-Maydani). The editor states that he collected the earliest and most reliable manuscripts of both works, as well as numerous commentaries on al-Quduri, to establish the most correct text. He acknowledges the extensive textual variants between copies—due to reasons to be explained—and notes that he only comments on important ones. The passage reflects the meticulous scholarly approach typical of modern critical editions of classical Hanafi fiqh texts.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise manual of Hanafi fiqh by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a foundational text for the school.
اللباب (al-Lubab): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (d. 1298 AH), known as al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab.
النسخ الخطية (al-nusukh al-khattiyyah): Handwritten manuscript copies of the texts used by the editor for comparison.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preface, why does the editor omit many textual variants from his footnotes?
A) He did not have enough time to record them all.
B) He considers them unimportant for establishing the correct text.
C) The publisher limited the number of footnotes.
D) He only records variants that support his preferred reading.

Key Takeaway
Critical editions are essential for ensuring that the texts we rely on for fiqh rulings accurately reflect the author's original work.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Understanding Critical Edition of Hanafi Texts
Editorial methodology for critical edition of Hanafi fiqh texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why critical editions of classical Hanafi texts are essential for accurate fiqh rulings and identify the types of textual variants that can affect legal conclusions.

Core Idea
A single missing word in a manuscript can change a fiqh ruling — textual accuracy is foundational to legal reliability.

This passage is the editor's preface to a critical edition of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Lubab. While it contains no fiqh rulings, it reveals the painstaking work behind the text you study. Understanding this methodology gives you confidence in the transmitted rulings and alerts you to the fact that even classical texts require careful verification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's primary goal
Read the first paragraph to determine what the editor set out to achieve. He aimed to establish the sound and correct text of both Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Lubab by collecting the oldest and most accurate manuscripts.
The goal is to produce a reliable text for study and reference.
2
Recognize the types of textual variants
The editor describes variants as differences in wording, expression, omissions, additions of letters, words, sentences, or even entire rulings, conditions, or stipulations. Note the range: from minor to significant.
Variants can be grammatical, substantive, or legal in nature.
3
Understand the editor's selection criteria
The editor strove to record what he deemed correct or most correct. He did not annotate every variant, only important ones, to avoid burdening the reader. He also prepared a special study of seventeen examples showing variant impact.
The editor exercises ijtihad in choosing the preferred reading.
4
Note the impact on fiqh rulings
The editor explicitly states that textual variation can affect juristic rulings or attribution of opinions to Hanafi imams. This shows that manuscript accuracy directly influences the substance of fiqh.
A variant could change which opinion is attributed to Abu Hanifa, for example.
5
Appreciate the scholarly effort
The editor verified citations from original sources, corrected distortions, and kept footnotes light. Reflect on the dedication required to produce a trustworthy edition of these foundational texts.
This effort ensures that the rulings you study are based on the best available evidence.

تمهيد
عملي في خدمة اللباب ومختصر القدوري ومنهجي في التحقيق
وقد جعلتُ بيان ذلك في ثلاث وعشرين فقرة، وهي: ۱ - قمتُ بجَمْع ما تيسر من أقدم النسخ الخطية لمختصر القدوري وأدقها وأنفَسها، وكذلك جمعتُ نُسَخ اللباب المخطوطة والمطبوعة في زمن المؤلف وما بعده، وكذلك حصلت بفضل الله على أكبر قدر ممكن من شروح القدوري المخطوطة والمطبوعة، وبعدها اجتهدت في إثبات النص السليم الصحيح، أو الأصح، وذلك في كـل مـن مختصر القدوري، واللباب. ٢- إن فوارق النسخ في كل من الكتابين كثيرة وكثيرة جداً، لأسباب يأتي بيانها، ولذا لم أنبه عليها في تعليقاتي إلا ما كان مهماً منها، وتدعو الحاجة للإشارة إليها.
وهذه الفوارق بالنسبة لنسخ القدوري خاصة، قد تكون في اختلاف صياغة اللفظ، أو التعبير، وقد تكون في نقصان أو زيادة حرف أو كلمة أو جملة، أو أكثر، أو زيادة حكم أو قيد أو شرط، وهكذا مما يقل أو يكثر أهمية واعتباراً، وقد أثبت ما اجتهدت أنه من نص القدوري، وما هو الصحيح أو الأصح من النص، وطويت كثيراً
من التعليقات التي كتبتها أولاً لبيان فوارق النسخ، لعدم إشغال القارئ بها ، ولو أردت تسجيلها كلها، لطال الأمر كثيراً.
عند مقابلتي لنُسَخ القدوري المختلفة أثبتُ ما اجتهدت أنه من مختصر القدوري وإن لم يكن مُثبتاً في نسخة الميداني التي اعتمدها هو في شرح اللباب، وعليه جعلتُ نص القدوري الذي هو في أعلى الصفحات، هو هو بعينه المضمَّن في نص اللباب، ولم أنبه في الحاشية إلى ذلك إلا قليلاً؛ للاختلاف الكثير في نسخ القدوري، مجتهداً إثبات النص الصحيح، أو ما هو الأصح والأولى.
٤ـ من خلال عملي في مختصر القدوري تبين لي أمر مهم جداً، وهو الاختلاف الكبير القديم بين نُسَخه، مما له أثر كبير في اختلاف الحكم الفقهي، أو نسبة الأقوال لأئمة المذهب، وغير هذا، ولذا عقدت دراسةً خاصةً لذلك في مبحث خاص، وذكرت فيه سبعة عشر مثالاً مهماً، مع بيان اهتمام علماء المذهب والشراح بذلك، وكشفهم لها، وتوجيههم لنصها، وبيانهم للصحيح منها أو الأصح.
ه لم أنبه في الحاشية على ما وقفتُ عليه من أسقاط وتحريفات كثيرة في النسخ المخطوطة والمطبوعة لكتاب اللباب إلا نادراً لفائدة؛ تخفيفاً من الحواشي، وذلك بعد الاجتهاد والتأكد من صحة النص. ٦- راجعتُ النصوص التي نقلها الميداني من مصادرها مباشرةً أو بالواسطة، وذلك فيما يسر الله لي من الكتب المخطوطة أو المطبوعة، للتأكد من صحة النص، وبذلك انكشفت لى أمور كثيرة تم تداركها بتوفيق الله، وأثبت الصواب الصحيح منها.
Preface: Practical work in serving al-Lubab and Mukhtasar al-Quduri and my methodology in verification. I have placed its explanation in twenty-three paragraphs, which are: 1 - I collected what was available of the oldest manuscript copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, the most accurate and precious, and likewise collected the manuscript and printed copies of al-Lubab from the author's time and after, and likewise obtained, by the grace of God, as many manuscript and printed commentaries of al-Quduri as possible. After that, I strove to establish the sound and correct text, or the most correct, in both Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Lubab. 2 - The textual variants in each of the two books are many, very many, for reasons that will be explained later, and thus I did not point them out in my notes except what was important and necessitated reference. These variants, especially for the copies of al-Quduri, may be in differences of wording or expression, and may be in omission or addition of a letter, word, sentence or more, or addition of a ruling, condition or stipulation, and so on, varying in importance and consideration. I have recorded what I endeavored to be from the text of al-Quduri and what is correct or more correct of the text, and I set aside many of the notes I first wrote to explain textual variants so as not to burden the reader, and if I wanted to record them all, it would have become very lengthy. When I collated the various copies of al-Quduri, I recorded what I endeavored to be from Mukhtasar al-Quduri even if it was not recorded in the copy of al-Maydani that he relied upon in his commentary al-Lubab. Accordingly, I made the text of al-Quduri that is at the top of the pages exactly the same as that included in the text of al-Lubab, and I only rarely noted that in the margin due to the many differences in the copies of al-Quduri, striving to record the correct text or what is more correct and preferable. 4 - Through my work on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a very important matter became clear to me: the great and ancient variation among its copies, which has a significant impact on the difference in juristic rulings or attribution of opinions to the imams of the school, and so on. Therefore, I devoted a special study to that in a particular section, and I mentioned seventeen important examples in it, along with an explanation of the attention given by the scholars of the school and commentators to that, their uncovering of them, their direction of their text, and their clarification of what is correct or more correct among them. 5 - I did not point out in the margin what I came across of many omissions and distortions in the manuscript and printed copies of the book al-Lubab except rarely, for benefit, to keep the footnotes light, after striving and ensuring the correctness of the text. 6 - I verified the texts that al-Maydani transmitted from their sources directly or indirectly, from what God made easy for me of manuscript or printed books, to ensure the correctness of the text. By that, many things were uncovered for me that were rectified by God's grace, and I recorded the correct and sound among them.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This is a front matter passage from the editor's introduction to the critical edition of al-Lubab and Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The editor outlines his methodology in twenty-three paragraphs, of which six are detailed here. He first describes collecting the oldest and most accurate manuscripts of both texts, as well as commentaries on al-Quduri. He then notes the abundance of textual variants in both works and explains that he only annotated the important ones to avoid burdening the reader. For Mukhtasar al-Quduri, he compared multiple copies and established the text he deemed most correct, even if it differed from al-Maydani's base copy. He additionally prepared a special study of seventeen examples showing how textual variants affect legal rulings or attribution of opinions to Hanafi imams. He also mentions that he rarely noted omissions and distortions in al-Lubab manuscripts to keep footnotes minimal. Finally, he verified al-Maydani's citations by consulting original sources, uncovering and correcting many errors. This passage is strictly editorial and contains no substantive fiqh rulings; it provides the reader with confidence in the editor's method.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise fiqh manual by Imam Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a foundational text of the Hanafi school, the subject of this critical edition.
اللباب (al-Lubab): The commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Maydani (d. 1298 AH), itself a standard reference, which the editor is now critically editing.
فوارق النسخ (fawariq al-nusakh): Variant readings among different manuscript copies of the same text, which the editor compares to establish the correct version.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The critical edition of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Lubab ensures that the transmitted fiqh rulings are based on the most reliable manuscripts, accounting for textual variants that could change legal conclusions.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The Editor's Methodology in al-Lubab
Editor's methodological introduction to al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the key principles of textual criticism in the Hanafi tradition as practiced by the editor of al-Lubab, and apply them to evaluate the reliability of a given text.

Core Idea
The editor's task is to reconstruct the authentic text and highlight the relied-upon fatwa from among variant manuscripts.

In this lesson, we step back from substantive fiqh to examine how Hanafi scholars ensure the integrity of the texts they study. The editor of al-Lubab, a standard commentary on al-Quduri, describes his method for comparing manuscripts, verifying sources, and determining the mu'tamad. Understanding this methodology is essential for anyone who wishes to engage critically with Hanafi primary sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's primary sources and approach
Note that the editor worked with multiple manuscripts of al-Quduri and al-Maydani's commentary. He sought to establish the correct text even when it differed from the copy used by al-Maydani.
This reflects a common practice: later editors do not blindly follow the commentator but use independent manuscript evidence.
2
Analyze the editor's handling of textual variants
He acknowledges significant variations among manuscripts and discusses their impact on fiqh rulings and attributions to madhhab imams. He mentions a separate study with 17 examples.
Variants can affect the hukm itself, not just the wording.
3
Examine the editor's verification of quotations
He checked al-Maydani's quotations against original sources, both manuscript and printed, to correct errors.
This is a standard critical edition practice.
4
Understand the editor's presentation choices
He divided the text into paragraphs, added headings, rarely cited page numbers in footnotes, and provided vocalization for difficult words. He also explained ancient measurements and places.
These choices aim to make the text accessible while preserving scholarly rigor.
5
Focus on the principle of mu'tamad al-mufta bihi
The editor paid special attention to identifying the relied-upon fatwa in cases of ikhtilaf among Hanafi imams.
This is the most important practical outcome for the student of fiqh.

من التعليقات التي كتبتها أولاً لبيان فوارق النسخ، لعدم إشغال القارئ بها ، ولو أردت تسجيلها كلها، لطال الأمر كثيراً.
عند مقابلتي لنُسَخ القدوري المختلفة أثبتُ ما اجتهدت أنه من مختصر القدوري وإن لم يكن مُثبتاً في نسخة الميداني التي اعتمدها هو في شرح اللباب، وعليه جعلتُ نص القدوري الذي هو في أعلى الصفحات، هو هو بعينه المضمَّن في نص اللباب، ولم أنبه في الحاشية إلى ذلك إلا قليلاً؛ للاختلاف الكثير في نسخ القدوري، مجتهداً إثبات النص الصحيح، أو ما هو الأصح والأولى.
٤ـ من خلال عملي في مختصر القدوري تبين لي أمر مهم جداً، وهو الاختلاف الكبير القديم بين نُسَخه، مما له أثر كبير في اختلاف الحكم الفقهي، أو نسبة الأقوال لأئمة المذهب، وغير هذا، ولذا عقدت دراسةً خاصةً لذلك في مبحث خاص، وذكرت فيه سبعة عشر مثالاً مهماً، مع بيان اهتمام علماء المذهب والشراح بذلك، وكشفهم لها، وتوجيههم لنصها، وبيانهم للصحيح منها أو الأصح.
ه لم أنبه في الحاشية على ما وقفتُ عليه من أسقاط وتحريفات كثيرة في النسخ المخطوطة والمطبوعة لكتاب اللباب إلا نادراً لفائدة؛ تخفيفاً من الحواشي، وذلك بعد الاجتهاد والتأكد من صحة النص. ٦- راجعتُ النصوص التي نقلها الميداني من مصادرها مباشرةً أو بالواسطة، وذلك فيما يسر الله لي من الكتب المخطوطة أو المطبوعة، للتأكد من صحة النص، وبذلك انكشفت لى أمور كثيرة تم تداركها بتوفيق الله، وأثبت الصواب الصحيح منها.

تمهید
لم ألتزم الإحالة والعزو بالجزء والصفحة للمصادر التي نقل
عنها المؤلف، تخفيفاً من الحواشي.
شرحت من الكلمات والعبارات ما رأيتُ الحاجة داعية إلى إيضاحه وبيانه من غير إطالة في الغالب، وذلك بتعليقات لطيفة
وإفادات مستحسنة، مع ذكر المصدر الذي نقلتُ عنه في ذلك. ٩- قمت ببيان المصطلحات القديمة للمسافات والمقادير المذكورة، وربطتها بالمصطلحات الحديثة؛ ليتم فهمها ومعرفتها، وكذلك الحال فيما ذكر من الأماكن والبلدان غير المشهورة.
١٠ - ضبطت ما يُشكل من النص، وما يحتاجه المتوسط إلى معرفة ضبطه، وقد استفدت كثيراً في هذا من نُسخ القدوري المخطوطة المضبوطة بالشكل ، ومن الضبط الذي استفدته من شيخنا العلامة الشيخ عبد الغفار الدروبي رحمه الله حين قرأتُ عليه
اللباب.
۱۱- قمت بتفقير نص اللباب إلى فقرات مرتبة، تساعد على فهمه وظهوره حساً ، ومعنى، وقمت بتقسيم مسائله، وتفصيلها إلى عدة مسائل ؛ لتكون أسرع فهماً ، وأسهل ضبطاً، وأيسر حفظاً، فتكثر الفائدة، وتتوفر العائدة، وجعلت للمسائل كلها إلا قليلاً عناوين جانبية كعلم بارز يُرشد إليها ، أو أكتفي بوضع نجمة في بداية المسألة لإظهارها، أو عند ذكر قول من الأقوال.
١٢ - اعتنيت كثيراً بمتابعة وذكر المعتمد المفتى به في المذهب في مسائل القدوري واللباب حال اختلاف أئمة المذهب فيها، وذلك
Introduction
13
From the comments I wrote first to explain the differences between manuscripts, so as not to distract the reader with them, and if I had wanted to record them all, it would have been too lengthy.
When collating the various copies of al-Quduri, I established what I endeavored to be from Mukhtasar al-Quduri even if it was not recorded in the copy of al-Maydani that he relied upon in his commentary of al-Lubab. Accordingly, I made the text of al-Quduri, which is at the top of the pages, exactly the same as the text incorporated in the text of al-Lubab, and I rarely alerted to that in the footnotes due to the great variation in the copies of al-Quduri, endeavoring to establish the correct text, or the most correct and preferable.
4. Through my work on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a very important matter became clear to me: the great ancient variation among its copies, which has a significant impact on differences in fiqh rulings or the attribution of statements to the imams of the madhhab, and other things. Therefore, I conducted a special study on this in a specific section, mentioning seventeen important examples, along with explaining the attention of the madhhab scholars and commentators to that, their uncovering of them, their guidance on their text, and their clarification of the sound or most sound among them.
5. I rarely alerted in the footnotes to the many omissions and distortions I found in the manuscript and printed copies of al-Lubab except rarely for a benefit, to lighten the footnotes, and that after exertion and verification of the correctness of the text. 6. I reviewed the texts that al-Maydani quoted from their original sources directly or indirectly, as far as God facilitated for me from manuscript or printed books, to verify the correctness of the text, and by that many matters were revealed to me that were rectified by God's grace, and I recorded the correct and sound among them.

Introduction
14
I did not commit to referencing and citing by volume and page number for the sources from which the author quoted, to lighten the footnotes.
I explained from the words and phrases what I saw the need to clarify and explain, without prolonging mostly, with nice comments and approved benefits, mentioning the source from which I quoted that. 9. I explained the ancient terms for distances and measurements mentioned, and connected them to modern terms so that they may be understood and known, and similarly for the places and countries mentioned that are not well-known.
10. I vocalized what is ambiguous in the text and what the intermediate student needs to know its vocalization, and I benefited greatly in this from the manuscripts of al-Quduri that are fully vocalized, and from the vocalization I benefited from our teacher, the scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghaffar al-Darubi (may God have mercy on him) when I read al-Lubab to him.
11. I divided the text of al-Lubab into ordered paragraphs that help in understanding it and its apparent clarity, both in form and meaning, and I divided its issues and detailed them into several issues to be faster to understand, easier to master, and simpler to memorize, so that benefit multiplies and returns are abundant. I gave all issues except a few side headings like a prominent banner guiding to them, or I sufficed with placing a star at the beginning of the issue to display it, or when mentioning a statement among the statements.
12. I paid great attention to following and mentioning the relied-upon fatwa in the madhhab regarding the issues of al-Quduri and al-Lubab when there is disagreement among the imams of the madhhab therein.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction (tamheed) to his work on al-Lubab, the commentary by al-Maydani on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The editor explains his methodology for establishing the correct text of al-Quduri, noting that he compared multiple manuscripts and prioritized what he determined to be the authentic text, even if it differed from the copy used by al-Maydani. He highlights the significant variations among manuscripts that affect fiqh rulings and attributions to madhhab imams, and he conducted a separate study with seventeen examples. To avoid burdening the reader, he rarely comments on omissions and distortions in the footnotes. He verified al-Maydani's quotations against original sources where possible. He also explains his approach to referencing (not citing volume and page), explaining difficult terms (including ancient measurements and obscure places), providing vocalization for ambiguous words, structuring the text into numbered paragraphs with headings, and especially noting the relied-upon fatwa (mu'tamad) in cases of ikhtilaf. This is typical of later Hanafi editors who aim to make the classical texts accessible while preserving the madhhab's authoritative positions.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise fiqh manual by Imam Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a foundational text in the Hanafi madhhab.
اللباب (al-Lubab): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (d. 1298 AH), which explains and expands upon the rulings of al-Quduri.
المعتمد المفتى به (al-mu'tamad al-mufta bihi): The relied-upon opinion in the madhhab for issuing fatwa, chosen from among the positions of the imams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the editor, what was his primary reason for not recording all manuscript variants in the footnotes?
A) He found no variants.
B) To lighten the footnotes and avoid distracting the reader.
C) The variants were all unimportant.
D) He did not have enough time.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi textual editor's role is to reconstruct the most authentic text and clarify the relied-upon fatwa, balancing thoroughness with accessibility.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Editorial Methodology in Hanafi Text: Mu'tamad and Takhrij
Editor's methodological principles for the edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the editor's approach to identifying the mu'tamad (relied-upon position) and authenticating hadiths (takhrij) in a classical Hanafi text.

Core Idea
A scholarly edition clarifies the mufta bihi and verifies hadiths, preserving the madhhab's integrity.

The editor of al-Lubab, Said Bakdash, outlines his careful methodology. He prioritizes the mu'tamad (the relied-upon ruling) when Hanafi imams differ, and authenticates hadiths even those missed by earlier scholars. This lesson explores why such editorial work is essential for reliable fiqh practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's primary goals
Read points 12 and 16 from the passage. The editor states he focuses on the mu'tamad and authenticates hadiths. These are his two main methodological commitments.
He mentions completing the work of al-Maydani (point 12).
2
Understand the concept of mu'tamad
The editor explains that when the Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) differ, he traces the mu'tamad from later reliable books. This is essential for fatwa.
Mu'tamad is not necessarily the majority view; it is the view chosen by later scholars for its strength.
3
Analyze the takhrij process
The editor mentions authenticating hadiths from al-Lubab, especially those from al-Hidayah that were not previously traced by al-Zayla'i and others.
Takhrij involves tracing the source and assessing authenticity using the criteria of hadith scholars.
4
Evaluate boundaries of the edition
Point 15 shows the editor stays within Hanafi fiqh, only mentioning other schools when the author himself does. This respects the nature of the text.
A modern editor must decide when to expand beyond the original scope.

١٢ - اعتنيت كثيراً بمتابعة وذكر المعتمد المفتى به في المذهب في مسائل القدوري واللباب حال اختلاف أئمة المذهب فيها، وذلك
بتتبع من يهتم بذلك من كتب المذهب، إتماماً لما قام به الميداني. ١٣ - قمت بالتدليل لمسائل قليلة من اللباب بشكل مختصر إذا رأيت الحاجة داعيةً لذلك، وذلك بالرجوع إلى كتب المذهب التي تعتني بذكر الدليل.
١٤ ـ أضفت في تعليقاتي مسائل فقهية قليلة، زيادة علـى مـا في اللباب، معزوةً لمن نَقلتُها عنه، رأيتُ الحاجة داعية إلى إلحاقها، إتماماً للفائدة المرجوة، مع علمي بأن مسائل الفقه كثيرة لا تُحصى، ولا يتسع المقام للزيادات ١٥ - لما كان كتاب اللباب كتاباً خاصاً بالفقه الحنفي، لذا أبقيته كما أراد مؤلّفه، ولم أتعرض فيما علقت عليـه لـذكر أقوال بقية أ المذاهب الأربعة، لئلا يخرج الكتاب عما أراده مؤلفه.
وفي حال تعرض المؤلف لذكر قول غير الحنفية، وهذا قليل جداً، أقوم بتوثيق تلك الأقوال من الكتب المعتمدة في تلـك
المذاهب.
مع
١٦ ـ قمت بتخريج الأحاديث المذكورة في اللباب بدون إطالة، الاجتهاد في البحث عن حكمها وبيان درجتها إن لم تكن في
الصحيحين، وذلك من خلال أقوال أئمة أهل الشأن في ذلك.
وقد وفقني الله تعالى بفضله وكرمه للوقوف على نقول مهمة في الحكم على الأحاديث، وكذلك في تخريج أحادي أحاديث ذكرت في الهداية، ونقلها صاحب اللباب وفات تخريجها حتى عند من خرج أحاديث الهداية، كالزيلعي، وغيره من شراح الهداية.
Introduction
I did not commit to referencing and citing by volume and page for the sources from which the author transmitted, to lighten the footnotes. I explained the words and phrases that I saw need for clarification and exposition without prolongation for the most part, by means of fine comments and beneficial notes, mentioning the source from which I transmitted that. 9- I explained the ancient terms for distances and measurements mentioned, and linked them to modern terms, so that they may be understood and known, and similarly for places and countries that are not well-known.
10- I voweled what is ambiguous in the text, and what the intermediate student needs to know its voweling, and I benefited much in this from the manuscripts of al-Quduri that are voweled, and from the voweling I learned from our teacher, the great scholar Shaykh Abd al-Ghaffar al-Darubi (may Allah have mercy on him) when I read to him al-Lubab.
11- I divided the text of al-Lubab into ordered paragraphs that help in understanding it and make it appear clearly, in form and meaning, and I divided its issues and detailed them into several sub-issues, to be faster to understand, easier to master, and simpler to memorize, so that benefit multiplies and advantage is obtained. I gave to all but a few issues side headings as a prominent marker guiding to them, or I sufficed with placing a star at the beginning of the issue to show it, or when mentioning a saying among the sayings.
12- I paid much attention to following and mentioning the relied-upon position (mu'tamad) in the school in the issues of al-Quduri and al-Lubab where the imams of the school differed, by tracing those who care about that from the books of the school, completing what al-Maydani did.
13- I provided evidence for a few issues from al-Lubab briefly when I saw a need for that, by referring to the books of the school that care about mentioning the evidence.
14- I added in my comments a few fiqh issues, beyond what is in al-Lubab, attributed to the one from whom I transmitted them, when I saw a need to append them, to complete the desired benefit, while knowing that fiqh issues are many and cannot be counted, and the context does not allow for additions.
15- Since the book al-Lubab is a book specific to Hanafi fiqh, I kept it as its author intended, and I did not address in my comments the mention of the views of the rest of the four schools, lest the book go beyond what its author intended. However, if the author mentions a non-Hanafi view, which is very rare, I document those views from the reliable books of those schools.
16- I authenticated the hadiths mentioned in al-Lubab without prolongation, striving to research their ruling and clarify their grade if they are not in the two Sahihs, through the statements of the leading scholars in that field. And Allah has enabled me by His bounty and generosity to come across important quotes regarding the judgment on hadiths, as well as in authenticating hadiths mentioned in al-Hidayah that the author of al-Lubab transmitted and whose authentication was missed even by those who authenticated the hadiths of al-Hidayah, like al-Zayla'i and other commentators of al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction, specifically a numbered list of his methodological principles. He begins by explaining his approach to referencing: he avoids citing specific volume and page numbers to keep footnotes minimal. He then clarifies that he explains only words and phrases needing clarification, doing so briefly with references. In point 9, he converts ancient measurements to modern ones. In point 10, he describes how he relied on voweled manuscripts and his teacher's guidance. Point 11 explains his division of the text into paragraphs and sub-issues with headings or stars for clarity. Point 12 is crucial: he states his focus on identifying the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position within the Hanafi school when there is ikhtilaf among the imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). He completes the work of al-Maydani. Point 13 says he occasionally provides brief evidence for rulings. Point 14 notes he adds a few extra fiqh issues from other sources. Point 15 emphasizes that he keeps the work strictly Hanafi, only documenting non-Hanafi views when the author himself mentions them. Finally, point 16 describes his hadith authentication work, particularly for hadiths from al-Hidayah that al-Lubab quotes but had not been previously authenticated, even by specialists like al-Zayla'i. This introduction demonstrates the editor's scholarly rigor and commitment to the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
المعتمد المفتى به (al-mu'tamad al-mufta bihi): The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school according to which fatwa is given, especially when there is ikhtilaf among the founding imams.
تخريج الأحاديث (takhrij al-ahadith): The process of tracing hadiths to their original sources, verifying their authenticity, and grading them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the editor (Said Bakdash) not include the views of the other three schools in his commentary?
A) He did not know them.
B) The book al-Lubab is specifically Hanafi, and he wanted to keep it as its author intended.
C) He considered only the Hanafi school to be correct.
D) The other schools' views were not relevant to the topics covered.

Key Takeaway
A scholarly edition of a Hanafi text requires identifying the mu'tamad for fatwa and authenticating hadith evidence, all while respecting the original work's scope.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Editor's Methodology for Hanafi Fiqh and Hadith Evidence
Editorial introduction explaining methodology for proofs, hadith, and school boundaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between the method of Hanafi jurists and hadith scholars in accepting hadith, and identify how the editor of al-Lubab approaches evidence and school boundaries.

Core Idea
The Hanafi method of hadith acceptance differs from muhaddithin; rulings stand on established school positions.

This passage is the editor's introduction to the critical edition of al-Lubab. He explains his methodology: providing evidence, adding fiqhi notes, staying within the Hanafi school, and performing takhrij of hadith using the method of the fuqaha. He also critiques a previous editor who improperly rejected Hanafi rulings based on weak hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's goal
The editor aims to complete al-Maydani's work by providing brief evidence for rulings and adding occasional fiqhi notes, but always stays within the Hanafi school as intended by the original author.
2
Understand the distinction in hadith methodology
The editor quotes Imam al-Jassas, who states that the fuqaha do not rely on the method of muhaddithin. Acceptance of hadith in Hanafi fiqh follows its own ijtihad-based principles.
This is a key methodological point: a hadith graded weak by muhaddithin may still be used by Hanafi jurists.
3
Note the editor's takhrij approach
The editor performed takhrij for hadith in al-Lubab, consulting works like 'al-Asl' by Imam Muhammad and al-Hidayah commentaries. He discovered important chains not found by others.
His approach shows that takhrij for Hanafi fiqh requires consulting sources that uphold the fuqaha method.
4
Recognize the critique of a previous editor
The editor criticizes an editor of 'al-Ikhtiyar' who rejected Hanafi rulings based solely on his own hadith grading. This highlights the danger of applying muhaddithin criteria without understanding the school's evidentiary hierarchy.
The critique underscores the necessity of respecting the madhhab's established positions.
