The Scholar's Library: Al-Maydani and Ibn 'Abidin's Legacy
Biographical account of the author and his teacher's library.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the preservation of Ibn 'Abidin's library by al-Maydani exemplifies the Hanafi tradition of scholarly transmission (riwaya) and identify the importance of specialized libraries for fatwa and research.

Core Idea
A scholar's library is the living chain of transmission — al-Maydani preserved Ibn 'Abidin's collection to guard the Hanafi legacy.

This passage from the introduction to al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri introduces us to the author, Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, and the remarkable story of his library. It was originally amassed by his teacher, the great Hanafi jurist Ibn 'Abidin, and then purchased by al-Maydani when the heirs sought to sell it. This act of loyalty ensured that thousands of volumes on Hanafi fiqh remained intact for future scholars. Understanding the role of such libraries helps us appreciate the physical and intellectual continuity of the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key figures
Recognize Shaykh al-Maydani as the commentator of al-Lubab and Ibn 'Abidin as his teacher, the author of Radd al-Muhtar.
Al-Maydani is the author of the commentary; Ibn 'Abidin is the earlier authority whose works are central to later Hanafi fatwa.
2
Understand the library's origin
The library was collected by Ibn 'Abidin over many years; it was a comprehensive collection, especially strong in Hanafi fiqh.
The passage emphasizes that the library was 'valuable, precious, rich, rare, and distinctive.'
3
Analyze the act of preservation
When Ibn 'Abidin's heirs wanted to sell the library, al-Maydani bought the bulk of it out of loyalty (wafa') and piety (birr), preventing its dispersal.
This act reflects the strong teacher-student bond in the Hanafi tradition.
4
Connect to Hanafi transmission
The library served as a repository of Hanafi texts, enabling the continuity of knowledge. Without such preservation, many works might have been lost.
Transmission (riwaya) in fiqh relies on accurate texts passed from teacher to student.
5
Reflect on the value of specialized collections
A specialized library focusing on Hanafi works aided research and fatwa, giving al-Maydani's writings a distinct advantage.
The passage notes that such a library 'increases his scientific progress, activity, prominence, verification, and precision.'

مكتبة الشيخ الميداني
من المعلوم أن وجود مكتبة كبيرة نفيسة متخصصة لدى العالم المتيقظ النابه المنبه ، مما يزيد في تقدمه العلمي، ونشاطه وبـروزه، وتحقيقه وتدقيقه، ويكون لذلك الأثر الكبير في تميزه على غيره، كما يكسب مؤلفاته مزايا علمية خاصة لا تجدها عند غيره، وفوائد أخرى كثيرة غير هذا.

هذه المكتبة عَمِلَ على جَمْعها سنين طويلة شيخه العلامة ابن عابدين صاحب الحاشية المشهورة، ثم آل معظمها إلى تلميذه الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، وذلك حين أراد ورثةُ ابن عابدين بيعها، فكان من وفاء الميداني الشيخه وبره بأستاذه، أنه لم يرض بتفريط الورثة بتلك المكتبة العظيمة، وضياعها شَذَرَ مَذَرَ بأيدي التجار المشترين ، فاشترى غالبها ، والقسم الآخر اشتراه تلميذ ابن عابدين الآخر الشيخ محمد البيطار نجل الشيخ حسن البيطار.
Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. Peace be upon Jesus son of Mary upon him... [unclear] completion of this book Muhammad Allah Almighty and from His success by the hand of the poorest of servants and the most needing the intercession of the master of servants, 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, may his Lord grant him aspirations in the middle of the honored Sha'ban [unclear]... Image from the handwriting of Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, from al-A'lam of al-Zirikli, vol. 4 p. 34, manuscript from the Arab Library in Damascus. 125. 126. Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. Section Ten: The Library of Shaykh al-Maydani. It is known that the existence of a large, precious, specialized library with the alert, distinguished scholar increases his scientific progress, activity, prominence, verification, and precision, and has a great effect in his distinction over others, and also gives his writings special scientific advantages not found in others, and many other benefits besides. And indeed, among the favors with which Allah Almighty honored the scholar Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani is that He granted him a comprehensive, valuable, precious, rich, rare, and distinctive library that contained many books in various arts, especially in the Hanafi school. This library was collected over long years by his teacher, the scholar Ibn 'Abidin, author of the famous commentary (Hashiya), and then most of it passed to his student Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani when Ibn 'Abidin's heirs wanted to sell it. Out of al-Maydani's loyalty and piety towards his teacher, he could not bear the heirs' squandering of that great library and its scattered dispersal at the hands of merchant buyers, so he bought most of it, and the other part was bought by Ibn 'Abidin's other student, Shaykh Muhammad al-Bitar, son of Shaykh Hasan al-Bitar.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction (tarjama) from the commentary 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' by Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. It begins with an unclear invocation and a note about an image of the author's handwriting from al-Zirklili's biographical dictionary. The main content is the description of the author's library, which was originally collected by his teacher, the famous Hanafi jurist Ibn 'Abidin (author of 'Radd al-Muhtar'). When Ibn 'Abidin's heirs intended to sell the library, al-Maydani purchased most of it out of loyalty, preventing its dispersal. The remaining portion was bought by another student, Muhammad al-Bitar. This highlights the importance of scholarly libraries in the Hanafi tradition and the transmission of knowledge from teacher to student.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjama): Biographical entry or account of a person's life.
مكتبة (maktaba): A library or collection of books, here referring to the personal scholarly library of al-Maydani.
ابن عابدين (Ibn 'Abidin): Muhammad Amin ibn 'Abidin (d. 1252 AH/1836 CE), a leading Hanafi jurist known for his commentary 'Radd al-Muhtar 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Significance of Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and the Role of Al-Lubab
Front matter introducing al-Lubab and its relationship to al-Kitab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is a foundational text in the Hanafi school and describe how commentaries like Al-Lubab serve to elucidate it.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is the bedrock of Hanafi fiqh; commentaries like Al-Lubab unlock its depth and are essential for thorough understanding.

Before delving into the rulings of the Hanafi school, it is crucial to understand the textual tradition through which these rulings are transmitted. This lesson introduces you to two key works: the Mukhtasar of Imam al-Quduri (known as al-Kitab) and its famous commentary Al-Lubab. By grasping the relationship between a foundational matn and its sharh, you will appreciate how Hanafi fiqh has been preserved and taught for centuries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Text
Locate the name of the original work being commented on: Mukhtasar al-Quduri, also called al-Kitab. Note its author and date of death (428 AH).
Al-Kitab means 'the Book'—a title indicating its authoritative status.
2
Understand Its Authority in the Hanafi School
Recognize that this Mukhtasar is a concise summary of Hanafi fiqh and is considered a reliable text (matn matin) that has spawned many commentaries.
The text is so trusted that it became a standard curriculum item.
3
Identify the Commentary
Al-Lubab is a commentary (sharh) on al-Kitab. Its full title, Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab, means 'The Core in Explaining the Book.'
The author of this commentary is al-Maydani, who later explains his methodology.
4
Distinguish the Commentator's Introduction from the Original
In the passage, al-Maydani quotes al-Quduri's own introduction. Be careful not to attribute that quote to al-Maydani.
The quotation begins with 'Ammā ba‘d...' and describes the widespread acceptance of al-Kitab.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب
١٤١
المبحث الأول
التعريف بكتاب : اللباب في شرح الكتاب
وبيان عمل المؤلف ومنهجه فيه
اللباب هو شرح لمختصر الإمام القدوري أبي الحسين أحمـد بـن محمد، المتوفى سنة ٤٢٨ هـ ، وهو مختصر في الفقه الحنفي، ويسمى بـ «الكتاب»، وهو متن متين معتمد في المذهب الحنفي، وعليه شروح كثيرة، وسيأتي فصل خاص للكلام عنه.
وقد طبع «اللباب عدة طبعات في حياة المؤلف، وبعده، والطبعة المتداولة الآن في أربعة أجزاء، كل جزء منها يقع في حدود

قال :
... *
أما بعد : فإن الكتاب المبارك للإمام القدوري، قد شاعت بركته حتى صارت كالعلم الضروري ، ولذا عكفت الطلبة على تفهمه وتفهيمه، وازدحموا على تعلمه وتعليمه، وكنت ممن عكف عليه الأيام الكثيرة، ودأب على التردُّد إليه حتى أسر إليه ضميره، فرأيتُ
Chapter Two: Study of Al-Lubab
141
First Section
Definition of the book: Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab
And explanation of the author's work and his methodology therein
Al-Lubab is a commentary on the Mukhtasar of Imam al-Quduri Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad, who died in 428 AH. It is a summary of Hanafi fiqh, and is called 'al-Kitab.' It is a solid, relied-upon text in the Hanafi school, and there are many commentaries on it. A special chapter will come later to discuss it.
Al-Lubab has been printed several times during the author's life and after it. The current edition is in four volumes, each volume approximately 230 pages.
Before discussing the author's work in it and explaining his methodology and approach, I quote his introduction so that the reader may see from it what he himself stated in that regard, where he said:
... *
To proceed: The blessed book of Imam al-Quduri has spread its blessing until it became like necessary knowledge. Therefore, students devoted themselves to understanding it and making others understand it, and crowded around learning it and teaching it. I was among those who devoted themselves to it for many days and persistently returned to it until my inner self confessed to it, so I saw...
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is front matter from the commentary Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab. The author, al-Maydani, begins by introducing the book he is commenting on: the Mukhtasar of Imam al-Quduri. This Mukhtasar is a foundational text in the Hanafi school, often referred to simply as 'al-Kitab' (the Book) due to its authority. Al-Maydani notes that it has received many commentaries, and that Al-Lubab is one of them. He then gives publication details: the work has been printed multiple times, and the widely available edition spans four volumes of about 230 pages each. Before explaining his own methodology in writing this commentary, al-Maydani quotes the original introduction of al-Quduri to allow the reader to see the author's own words. The quoted excerpt from al-Quduri's introduction emphasizes the widespread acceptance and blessing of the Mukhtasar, describing it as necessary knowledge ('ilm daruri) that students eagerly studied and taught. Al-Maydani includes himself among those who devoted themselves to studying it deeply until its meaning became clear to him.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): The title of this commentary, meaning 'the core' or 'the essence'.
القدوري (al-Quduri): Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), the author of the Mukhtasar (also known as al-Kitab), a foundational Hanafi fiqh text.
الكتاب (al-Kitab): A name given to al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, meaning 'the Book' par excellence, indicating its authoritative status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Al-Lubab is a summary of Al-Kitab.
B) Al-Lubab is a commentary on Al-Kitab.
C) Al-Lubab and Al-Kitab are independent works.
D) Al-Kitab is a commentary on Al-Lubab.

Key Takeaway
Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is the cornerstone of Hanafi fiqh, and Al-Lubab is a key commentary that elucidates it.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Understanding al-Lubab: A Blended Hanafi Commentary
Introduction to al-Lubab and its author's methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the blended commentary method (sharh mazji) used in al-Lubab and identify its significance in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab blends al-Quduri's matn with seamless explanation — a model of accessible yet authoritative Hanafi commentary.

This lesson introduces you to the book al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab, a renowned commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. You will explore its author's purpose, his methodology of blended commentary (sharh mazji), and how this work became a cornerstone for Hanafi fiqh study. Understanding this background will help you appreciate the structure and authority of the texts you will encounter throughout this madrasa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text and commentary
Recognize that al-Lubab is a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. Note the full title: al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab. The base matn is called 'al-Kitab' or 'al-Mukhtasar'.
2
Understand the author's motivation
From the author's introduction, see his humility and his desire to clarify the Mukhtasar. He mentions that students crowded to learn it, and he wanted to serve the text by adding necessary explanations.
The author al-Maydani emphasizes his own shortcomings but is driven by hope for blessing.
3
Describe the sharh mazji method
Al-Maydani interweaves his own words with al-Quduri's original text so seamlessly that the reader experiences a continuous flow. This is the hallmark of a blended commentary (sharh mazji).
Contrast with separate commentaries where matn and sharh are visually distinct.
4
Recognize the sources used
The author collected from the words of earlier scholars, added what is needed, and incorporated selections from 'al-Tashih' by 'Allamah Qasim. He aimed to present the relied-upon (mufta bihi) positions.
This shows the work's authority and reliability.
5
Summarize the significance
Al-Lubab is a trusted commentary widely used in Hanafi circles. Its blended style makes it accessible for students while maintaining scholarly rigor.
The passage also notes it was printed multiple times, indicating its popularity.

The second chapter: Study of al-Lubab. 141. First topic: Definition of the book: al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab, and explanation of the author's work and his methodology in it. Al-Lubab is a commentary on the Mukhtasar of Imam al-Quduri Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad, who died in 428 AH. It is a compendium in Hanafi fiqh, called 'the Book'. It is a solid and relied-upon text in the Hanafi school, and there are many commentaries on it. A special chapter will come to discuss it. Al-Lubab has been printed in several editions during the author's life and after. The currently circulated edition is in four volumes, each of about 230 pages. Before speaking about the author's work in it, and explaining his methodology and approach, I quote his introduction so that the reader may see what he stated therein, where he said: ... 'Amma ba'd: Indeed the blessed book of Imam al-Quduri, its blessing has become widespread until it became like essential knowledge. Therefore, students devoted themselves to understanding it and making it understood, and crowded to learn it and teach it. I was among those who devoted many days to it and persisted in returning to it until its inner meaning was disclosed to me. So I saw some of its jewels hidden in their mines, and some of its subtleties concealed in their hiding places. It often occurred to me to intrude upon it by collecting some expressions that would serve as a commentary to it, to detail its summary, restrict its absolute, and clarify its meanings in a moderate manner, with clarification such that it would assist in its meanings, except that I was prevented because I am not among the people of this matter and have short reach in this field. Then I was impelled to enter this arena hoping to be associated by service to that Imam, clinging to the hem of his blessing, and seeking blessing by serving him. So I sought guidance from Allah, and I collected from their words what indicates their intent and purpose, with additions of what is likely to be needed, and seeking what is relied upon and the fatwa is given upon, and incorporating what the scholar Qasim compiled in his book 'al-Tashih' from the choices of the Imams for what is most preponderant and correct. I spared no effort in refining and editing, and seeking what is most apparent and clearest in expression...' End. Thus, through this introduction of the author and my long association with the book al-Lubab, my service to it, and verifying its text, I can explain the author's work therein, his methodology and approach in the following points: 1- Al-Lubab is a blended commentary between its wording and the wording of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, with complete mastery in this blending. So the reader mostly feels while reading al-Lubab only complete sequence and orderly harmony between the phrases of the Mukhtasar and the commentary, without any break or discord, and this requires 6.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is an introductory study (front matter) of the book al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Kitab by the Hanafi scholar al-Maydani. It first defines al-Lubab as a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text. The author then quotes al-Maydani's own introduction, where he describes the widespread acceptance of al-Quduri's work, his own humble motivation to write a commentary, and his methodology: he blended the matn (original text) and sharh (commentary) seamlessly, added necessary clarifications, relied on the most authoritative positions, and incorporated selections from the book al-Tashih by 'Allamah Qasim. The passage concludes with a summary analysis by the current editor: the work is a 'blended commentary' (sharh mazji) that interweaves the original text with explanation so smoothly that the reader experiences continuous, harmonious reading. This introduction sets the stage for understanding the nature and authority of al-Lubab in the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): The title of the commentary by al-Maydani on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar; literally 'the core' or 'the essence'.
القدوري (al-Quduri): Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), author of the Mukhtasar, a seminal Hanafi fiqh text.
شرح مزجي (sharh mazji): A blended commentary where the commentator interweaves his own words with the original matn seamlessly.
المختصر (al-Mukhtasar): Al-Quduri's concise fiqh compendium, also called 'al-Kitab'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Lubab is a blended commentary that seamlessly integrates al-Quduri's Mukhtasar with explanation, relying on authoritative sources, making it a key text for Hanafi fiqh study.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Author's Methodology in Al-Lubab: An Intermediate Commentary
Description of the author's methodology and features of Al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key characteristics of al-Maydani's commentary Al-Lubab and explain its methodology as an intermediate integrated commentary.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab is a seamless integrated commentary that is intermediate in length, prioritizing clarity and relied-upon positions.

Before diving into the legal rulings of the Hanafi school, it is essential to understand the tools and texts that transmit them. Al-Lubab, by Sheikh al-Maydani, is one of the most accessible commentaries on the foundational matn Mukhtasar al-Quduri. This lesson introduces the author's own description of his methodology: a carefully blended, intermediate commentary that adds necessary details and relies on authoritative sources. Understanding this methodology will help you navigate the text and appreciate its design for effective learning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of the commentary
Note that al-Maydani explicitly calls Al-Lubab a 'sharh mazji' (integrated commentary) and an intermediate commentary. Recognize that this means his words are interwoven with al-Quduri's text seamlessly, aiming for a balance between conciseness and detail.
The author states it is 'closer to conciseness than to length'.
2
Recognize the author's motive and sources
Al-Maydani explains he collected from earlier scholars' words, added what was needed, and relied on authoritative positions, especially from al-Qasim's 'Al-Tashih'. Note that he drew additional issues from 'Al-Hidayah', 'Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah', and 'Al-Durar wa al-Ghurar'.
His goal was to provide the relied-upon (mufta bihi) rulings.
3
Understand the structural features
Observe that al-Maydani explains the ordering of chapters (munasabat), gives linguistic and technical definitions, and corrects difficult words. These features make the commentary pedagogically useful.
He prioritizes clarity and ease of expression.
4
Appreciate the skill required
Reflect on the challenge of blending two texts seamlessly. The passage notes this requires strong mastery in expression and diverse knowledge, which al-Maydani possessed.
This integration is a hallmark of later Hanafi commentary tradition.

Chapter Two: A Study of Al-Lubab. Some of its jewels were hidden in their mines, and some of its subtleties were concealed in their hiding places. It often occurred to me to insert into it a collection of phrases that would serve as a commentary on it, to detail its summary, restrict its absolute, and clarify its meanings in a moderate manner, with clarification so that it would be an aid to its meanings, except that I was prevented by the fact that I am not among the people of this field and have a short reach in this arena. Thus, through the author's introduction and my long association with the book Al-Lubab, my service to it, and my editing of its text, I can explain the author's work in it, his methodology, and his method in the following points: 1 - Al-Lubab is an integrated commentary between his own expressions and the expressions of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, with perfect skill in this blending, so that the reader, while reading Al-Lubab, generally feels only complete continuity and harmonious orderly coherence between the expressions of the mukhtasar (abridgment) and the commentary, without any interruption or discord, and this requires strong mastery in expression that Sheikh al-Maydani was given, and the diverse knowledge he acquired helped him in that. 2 - Al-Lubab is an intermediate commentary, as its author stated in the introduction, and in its intermediateness it is closer to conciseness than to length. The commentator pursues in it what is most manifest and clear in expression, so this commentary is among the clearest and smoothest of commentaries. 4 - It was from the methodology of the commentator al-Maydani that he added many jurisprudential issues and branches to Mukhtasar al-Quduri, seeing the need to add them, and he mostly brings them from 'Al-Hidayah', 'Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah', and 'Al-Durar wa al-Ghurar'. 5 - The commentator al-Maydani is concerned with mentioning subtle occasions for the titles of the books and jurisprudential chapters found in Mukhtasar al-Quduri, linking them to each other, explaining without prolixity the reason for placing this before that and delaying that over something else, which is called the occasions for ordering topics. 6 - The commentator al-Maydani explains the linguistic meaning of the title of the book he is commenting on, then mentions the technical religious meaning. He is concerned with correcting difficult words in the text in a concise subtle manner, and explains the strange expressions that occur. And I note here that when al-Maydani inserts the words of his commentary among the words of Mukhtasar al-Quduri in the integrated commentary method, this often leads to... (the text cuts off).

Commentary
This passage is a study of the book 'Al-Lubab' by al-Maydani, which is a commentary on 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri', a foundational Hanafi fiqh text. The author of the study quotes al-Maydani's own introduction, where he explains his motivation and method. Al-Maydani describes himself as not being a master of this field initially, but he ventured to compile a commentary that would detail the concise statements of al-Quduri, clarify ambiguous expressions, and provide relied-upon rulings. He sought to include what is most needed and to follow the authoritative positions, especially drawing from the 'Tashih' of al-Qasim. The study then lists six characteristics of al-Maydani's commentary: 1) It is an 'integrated commentary' (sharh mazji) that seamlessly blends his own words with those of the Mukhtasar; 2) It is intermediate in length—closer to brevity than prolixity, yet clear; 3) It aims for the clearest expression; 4) It adds many additional fiqh issues from major Hanafi works like Al-Hidayah, Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, and Al-Durar wa al-Ghurar; 5) It explains the sequence of chapters and their interconnections (munasabat); 6) It provides linguistic definitions and corrects difficult words. The passage notes that this meticulous blending occasionally leads to... (text is cut off).

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): Title of al-Maydani's commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, meaning 'The Core' or 'The Essence'.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise Hanafi fiqh text by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely used as a foundational matn.
الشرح المزجي (al-sharh al-mazji): An integrated commentary where the commentator interweaves his own words with the original text seamlessly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Lubab is an intermediate integrated commentary that combines clarity, conciseness, and reliance on authoritative Hanafi sources.

Introduction and Front Matter

Methodology of Al-Lubab: Al-Maydani's Commentary on Al-Quduri
Describing the methodology of Al-Lubab commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the key methodological features of Al-Maydani's commentary Al-Lubab, including its medium length, added issues, use of munasabat, and preference for rational proofs.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab is a medium-length commentary that adds new fiqh issues, highlights topic order connections, and emphasizes rational proofs over transmitted ones.

This lesson introduces you to the methodology of Al-Lubab, a famous Hanafi commentary on Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. Understanding its features will help you navigate the text and appreciate its unique approach among Hanafi commentaries. The passage we study comes from a modern analysis of Al-Lubab's methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the commentary's length and style
The text states that Al-Lubab is a medium-length commentary, closer to brevity. Note that it is known for clarity and smoothness.
Medium-length means it is not as concise as the matn nor as expansive as some other commentaries.
2
Recognize additional sources used
Al-Maydani added many issues from later Hanafi works like Al-Hidayah, Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, and Durar wa Ghurar. Identify these sources.
This shows Al-Maydani's incorporation of later scholarship.
3
Understand the role of munasabat
Al-Maydani explains the logical or thematic connections between chapters and sections, justifying the ordering of topics. This is called 'munasabat tartib al-mawdu'at'.
This is a distinctive feature of Al-Lubab that aids comprehension.
4
Note the interwoven commentary and its effects
The commentary is written in an interwoven style (sharh mazji). This can change the vowelling and grammatical case of the original matn words, as illustrated by the example of 'wa al-satru afdal' becoming 'laakina al-satru afdal'.
Be aware that the vowelling in Al-Lubab may differ from standalone editions of Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
5
Analyze the evidentiary approach
Al-Maydani predominantly uses rational (aqli) proofs rather than transmitted (naqli) proofs, unlike Al-Hidayah which balances both. The text notes this contrast.
This reflects a different methodological emphasis; Al-Maydani focuses on dirayah (reasoning) over riwayah (transmission).

[He had] strong ability in expression that Sheikh Al-Maydani was given, and what he acquired from various sciences helped him in that. 2- Al-Lubab is a medium commentary, as its author stated in the introduction, and in its medium nature it is closer to brevity than to length. The commentator seeks therein the most apparent and clearest in expression, hence this commentary is among the clearest and smoothest commentaries. 4- It was from the methodology of commentator Al-Maydani that he added many juristic issues and branches to Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, which he saw a need to add, and he brings them mostly from Al-Hidayah, Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, and Durar wa Ghurar. 5- The commentator Al-Maydani pays attention to mentioning subtle connections (munasabat) for the titles of books and juristic chapters present in Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, linking them with each other, explaining without prolixity the reason for placing this before that and that after other, which is called 'munasabat tartib al-mawdu'at' (connections of ordering subjects). 6- The commentator Al-Maydani explains the linguistic meaning of the title of the book he is commenting on, then mentions the technical Shariah meaning. He pays attention to the correct vowelling of problematic words in the text in a subtle concise manner, and explains the uncommon expressions that occur. I note here that when Al-Maydani inserts the words of his commentary between the words of Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar in the interwoven commentary method, this often leads to changing the vowelling and parsing of the words of Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, due to the change in the position of the word. For example, Al-Quduri's statement: 'and covering is better', but in Al-Lubab it appears: 'but covering is better', and similar instances, sometimes causing the vowelling of the Mukhtasar recorded above to differ from the vowelling of the Mukhtasar scattered in Al-Lubab. - The commentator stated in the introduction that he pays attention to detailing its summaries, qualifying its unqualified, and clarifying its meanings in a moderate manner, and in all that he spared no effort in refining, editing, and correcting the expressions. 9- The commentator paid attention to providing evidence for the issues of Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, with transmitted and rational proofs, or what is called al-riwayah wa al-dirayah, but his predominant attention was to mentioning rational proofs. For when he quotes from Al-Hidayah explaining the issue and some of its proofs, you see him in most cases quoting rational proofs without transmitted ones, while the author of Al-Hidayah, from whom the author frequently quotes, was concerned with both aspects, so the author of Al-Hidayah strengthens transmitted knowledge (riwayah) with rational knowledge (dirayah) and vice versa. I thought much and researched the viewpoint of commentator Al-Maydani in this, but I found no explanation, and Allah knows best. And indeed, basing on transmitted proofs and then supporting them with rational proofs is what Imam al-Ayni considered good and urged, as he stated in the introduction of his book Al-Binayah, where he said: (1) 23/1 (Pakistan edition).
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a front_matter analysis describing the methodology of Al-Lubab, a commentary by Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani on Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The text highlights several key features: First, Al-Lubab is a medium-length commentary, closer to brevity, and is known for its clarity and smoothness. Second, Al-Maydani added many additional fiqh issues and sub-branches from authoritative Hanafi works like Al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani, Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah by al-Haddad, and Durar wa Ghurar by al-Haskafi. Third, he pays special attention to 'munasabat' — the subtle reasons for the ordering of chapters and topics in Al-Quduri's text, explaining why one topic precedes another. Fourth, he gives both linguistic (lughawi) and technical (shar'i) definitions for book titles. Fifth, he corrects vowelling and explains unusual words concisely. Sixth, the interwoven commentary style (sharh mazji) sometimes alters the original vowelling and grammatical case of Al-Quduri's words, as illustrated by the example: Quduri said 'and covering is better' whereas Al-Lubab has 'but covering is better' due to context. Finally, regarding proofs, Al-Maydani primarily offers rational (aqli) proofs rather than transmitted (naqli) ones, unlike the author of Al-Hidayah who balanced both. The author of this study notes that Al-Maydani's preference for rational proofs over transmitted ones contrasts with the methodology of Imam al-Ayni, who advocated starting with transmitted proofs and then supporting them with rational ones.

Key Terms
الشرح المزجي (al-sharh al-mazji): A commentary style where the commentator's words are inserted between the words of the original text (matn), merging the explanation with the original.
مناسبات ترتيب الموضوعات (munasabat tartib al-mawdu'at): The art of explaining the logical or thematic connections between chapters and sections of a book, justifying the order of presentation.
الرواية والدراية (al-riwayah wa al-dirayah): Transmitted knowledge (riwayah: textual proofs from Quran, hadith) and rational knowledge (dirayah: reasoning, qiyas, istihsan).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Rational proofs (aqli)
C) Both equally
D) Consensus (ijma')

Key Takeaway
Al-Lubab is characterized by its medium length, added issues from later sources, explanation of topic ordering, interwoven style, and preference for rational proofs.

Introduction and Front Matter

How Hanafi Commentaries Cite Proofs: A Methodological Guide
Methodological reflection on proof citation in Hanafi fiqh works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the proofs cited in Hanafi commentaries like al-Lubab are not exhaustive and how they serve to reassure the muqallid, and you will be able to identify the pitfalls of superficial comparative fiqh works.

Core Idea
Hanafi commentaries cite selective proofs to reassure, not to fully prove; real evidence is in extended works.

When you open a Hanafi fiqh commentary, you often see phrases like 'because' and 'indeed'. The author of al-Lubab explains that these proofs are not the complete set. They are chosen to illustrate reasoning and to comfort the follower. This lesson teaches you to read these citations correctly—as pedagogical tools, not as the full scholarly apparatus. It also warns against the common error of treating such citations as exhaustive when comparing madhhabs.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the Purpose of Proofs in Commentaries
Understand that commentaries like al-Lubab mention only some proofs. Their goal is to show that the rulings have a basis, not to present every evidence. This is for the muqallid's reassurance.
The author quotes a prior critic who says proofs come 'after establishing with report and textual specification'.
2
Identify the Source of Real Hanafi Evidence
The full proofs are in extended works (mabsutat) – both printed and manuscript. They include Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas with detailed explanation of wajh al-dalalah.
3
Distinguish Between Imam's Own Proof and Later Attribution
A proof cited for an imam's view may not be the imam's own original derivation. It could be a later scholar's attempt to support the madhhab. We cannot be certain unless explicitly stated.
This shows caution in historical attribution.
4
Understand the Reassurance Function
The proofs are meant to instill certainty in the follower that the rulings come from valid sources. This psychological effect repels doubts.
The author calls it 'scientia certitudinalis' (ilm al-yaqin).
5
Critique Superficial Comparative Fiqh
The author condemns works that cherry-pick proofs, hastily judge them weak, and declare preponderance without thoroughness. He also notes that jurists and hadith scholars have different standards for accepting hadith.
Al-Jassas is quoted: jurists do not rely on hadith scholars' principles exclusively.

Chapter Two: Study of al-Lubab. 145 ... 'Do you not see that most commentators of this book – al-Hidayah – and others among commentators of other works in this chapter have filled their writings with their saying 'because', and stuffed them with 'indeed', 'but', and this is only good after establishing with report and textual specification...' End quote. Based on this, what the author of al-Lubab mentions, and likewise other commentators of books, of proofs for the Hanafis, is only some of their proofs, so one should not limit oneself to them when citing evidence for the Hanafis. Whoever wants thorough investigation and comprehensive coverage, the extended Hanafi books, both printed and manuscript, are filled with proofs from the Book, Sunnah, consensus, and others, along with explaining the aspect of indication from the evidence, and other aspects of explaining the rules of deriving rulings from evidence. Also, the proofs mentioned in fiqh books for the statements of the imam of the madhhab – we cannot be certain that this is his proof that he used, and that this is his viewpoint in derivation. It may be this, and it may be something that was used to support his statement, and this is frequent. Likewise, the mention of some proofs for a statement is only to reassure the obligated follower of this madhhab, and to instill tranquility in his heart for what he does and performs of rulings, and so that he knows within himself with certain knowledge that these rulings are taken from various legislative sources, which have their sanctity, authority, and consideration, and that there is no ruling of any of the respected followed imams except that it has a proof and an aspect of indication, known to whoever knows it and unknown to whoever is ignorant of it. By that, the follower is repelled from the doubts of the doubters and the trials of the ignorant. 146 Chapter Two: Study of al-Lubab. Likewise, the issue of derivation is a very broad issue, requiring a separate specialized work, especially since every mujtahid imam has rules of derivation that differ from others. Also, the authentication and weakening of hadiths used as evidence is a matter of ijtihad, in which the views of hadith scholars differ. The method of jurists in accepting and rejecting reports is different from the method of hadith scholars. Imam Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas stated this in his Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, and others like Ibn Daqiq al-Id, Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani, and others. Rather, Imam al-Jassas says: 'We do not know any of the jurists who referred to them (hadith scholars) in accepting or rejecting reports, nor considered their principles.' End quote. Thus, there are many matters in derivation; the issue is not easy. Hence comes great astonishment at what some do in comparative fiqh research or in some comparative fiqh works, of mentioning some proofs for a statement without mentioning the rest of the proofs, and hastily judging them as weak, and then ruling with a stroke of a pen, without scientific integrity, for the preponderance of the other statement. Likewise, one is amazed at the broad titles given to books that contain some proofs, such as 'Islamic Fiqh and Its Proofs' or 'Maliki Fiqh and Its Proofs', and so on. (1) Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, beginning of Kitab al-Nikah, 4/244.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage serves as a methodological introduction (front matter) to the study of Hanafi fiqh. The author, al-Maydani, explains that the proofs cited by commentators like al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah and others are not exhaustive. They are selective examples meant to illustrate the reasoning, not to represent the full range of evidence. The true Hanafi proofs are extensive, found in longer works, covering Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and other sources with detailed explanations of their indication (wajh al-dalala). Moreover, the author warns against assuming that the proof cited for an imam's opinion is necessarily the imam's own original proof; it may be a later scholar's attempt to support the view. The purpose of citing these proofs is to reassure the lay follower (muqallid) that the rulings have solid evidentiary bases, not to provide complete academic proofs. The passage then critiques superficial comparative fiqh works that cherry-pick proofs, hastily deem them weak, and declare a preponderance without scholarly rigor. It also notes that jurists and hadith scholars have different criteria for accepting hadith, citing al-Jassas. This is a crucial reminder for students: the Hanafi madhhab has a vast and sophisticated usul al-fiqh, and reductionist presentations in modern 'fiqh and its proofs' books are often misleading.

Key Terms
الاستدلال (al-istidlāl): The process of deriving legal rulings from primary sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) using established principles of usul al-fiqh.
الدليل (al-dalīl): A piece of evidence from the Shariah sources that indicates a legal ruling. It can be from the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, or rational proof.
وجه الدلالة (wajh al-dalālah): The specific aspect or manner in which a proof indicates a ruling; the interpretive connection between the evidence and the derived law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the commentators intentionally hid the full proofs.
B) Because the authors only selected a few proofs to illustrate the reasoning and reassure the follower.
C) Because the Hanafi school has no proofs other than what is mentioned.
D) Because these books are meant only for advanced scholars.

Key Takeaway
The proofs in Hanafi commentaries are selective pedagogical tools; full evidence lies in extended works, and superficial citation in comparative studies is methodologically unsound.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Methodology of Selecting Authoritative Rulings in al-Lubab
Explains author's method for preferring strongest Hanafi positions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain al-Maidani's method for choosing the mufta bihi position when Hanafi imams differ, and identify his primary sources.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab prioritizes the strongest Hanafi position by relying on Tashih al-Quduri, not necessarily the earliest view.

The author of al-Lubab, al-Maidani, faced the challenge of presenting a concise fiqh manual while ensuring every ruling was the authoritative one within the Hanafi school. He did not simply repeat al-Quduri's text; he actively selected the strongest positions where the imams differed. This lesson explores his methodology and warns against the oversimplification seen in some modern comparative fiqh works.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the complexity of istidlal
Understand that different mujtahids have different principles of inference and that hadith criticism varies among scholars. This justifies al-Maidani's careful selection.
Al-Jassas emphasized that jurists do not blindly follow muhaddithin.
2
Identify the primary source: Tashih al-Quduri
Al-Maidani primarily relied on Qasim ibn Qutlubugha's work which compiled the preponderant choices of later Hanafi imams.
This shows that the mufta bihi may come from Abu Yusuf or Muhammad, not only Abu Hanifa.
3
Note the three modes of inclusion
Sometimes verbatim, often summarized, rarely omitted despite importance. This flexibility shows the author's independence.
4
Recognize supplementary sources
Al-Maidani also used al-Hidayah and Ibn Abidin's commentary to ensure accuracy.
These sources are authoritative in the later Hanafi tradition.
5
Apply the lesson: avoid hasty comparative fiqh
The author criticizes modern works that cite partial evidence and judge too quickly. Al-Maidani's careful approach is a model.

وطريقة الفقهاء في قبول الأخبار وردّها غير طريقة المحدثين ، وقد نص على هذا الإمام أبو بكر الرازي الجصاص في شرح مختصر الطحاوي، وغيره كابن دقيق العيد، وابن حجر العسقلاني وغيرهم، بل يقول الإمام الجصاص (۱) : ( ولا نعلم أحداً من الفقهاء رجع إليهم في قبول الأخبار وردها، ولا اعتبر أصولهم». اهـ
وهكذا أمور وأمور في الاستدلال، فالمسألة ليست بـالأمر السهل، ومن هنا يأتي العجب كل العجب، مما يفعله البعض في الأبحاث الفقهية المقارنة، أو في بعض المؤلفات الفقهية المقارنة، من ذكره لبعض الأدلة لقول ما دون ذكر بقية الأدلة، ويتسرع بالحكم عليها بالضعف، ومن ثم يقضي بشرطة قلم، وبدون أمانة علمية بالرجحان للقول الآخر؟!!
وكذلك يُتعجب مما يجعل من عناوين عريضة لكتب فيها بعض الأدلة، كالفقه الإسلامي وأدلته، أو : الفقه المالكي وأدلته، وهكذا.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب
١٤٧
۱۰ ـ اهتم صاحب اللباب كثيراً، بل تحرى ذِكْرَ الأصح والأقوى، والمعتمد المختار للفتوى، وذلك حال وجود خلاف بين أئمة المذهب في المسائل المذكورة، كما صرح بذلك في مقدمته. وكان اعتماده الأول في ذلك على كتاب العلامة قاسم بن قطلوبغا: «تصحيح القدوري»، وقد صرّح الميداني في مقدمة اللبــاب بضم ما جَمَعَه العلامة قاسم من اختيارات الأئمة لمـا هـو الراجح والصحيح. وهذا العمل الذي قام به العلامة قاسم عمل عظيم جليل، خَدَم به المذهب خدمة جليلة.
وهذا الضم والاحتواء من الميداني لتصحيح القدوري، يختلف قدره من مسألة لأخرى، فأحياناً يورد الميداني نصه كما هو، وأحياناً كثيرة يختصره، وفي أحيان قليلة يترك ذكره، مع كونه مهماً في تلك المسألة.
وبهذه المناسبة أشير إلى أني قد حاولت جاهداً إتمام مسيرة الميداني في بيان المعتمد المفتى به في المذهب فيما فاته، أو فيما فيه استدراك، أو اختلاف تصحيح، وذلك من «تصحيح القدوري»، ومن غيره من كتب المذهب المهتمة ببيان هذا الجانب.
كما اعتمد الميداني أيضاً على كتاب «الهداية» في بيان المفتى به، وعلى ما سجله شيخه العلامة ابن عابدين في حاشيته علـى الـدر المختار، فيأتي الميداني بخلاصات مما ذكره.
وهكذا كان يعتمد على كتاب «الجوهرة النيرة»، وعلى كتاب
Chapter Two: Study of al-Lubab. Thus the issue of istidlal is very broad, needing its own separate work, especially since each mujtahid imam has principles of deduction that differ from others. Likewise, authenticating and weakening hadiths used as evidence is an ijtihadi matter, in which the views of hadith scholars differ. The method of jurists in accepting and rejecting reports is not the method of hadith scholars. Imam Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas stated this in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, and others like Ibn Daqiq al-'Eid, Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani, etc. Rather, Imam al-Jassas said: 'We do not know any jurist who deferred to them in accepting or rejecting reports, nor considered their principles.' End quote. Thus there are many issues in istidlal; the matter is not easy. Hence astonishment comes at what some do in comparative fiqh research or in some comparative fiqh works: mentioning some evidence for a view without mentioning the rest of the evidence, hastily judging it weak, then ruling with a stroke of the pen, without scholarly integrity, for the other view. Likewise, one is astonished at the broad titles given to books containing some evidence, such as 'Islamic Fiqh and its Evidence' or 'Maliki Fiqh and its Evidence', etc. (1) Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, beginning of Kitab al-Nikah, 4/244. Chapter Two: Study of al-Lubab. 10. The author of al-Lubab paid great attention, indeed sought to mention the most sound and strongest, and the relied-upon chosen for fatwa, when there was a difference among the imams of the madhhab on the mentioned issues, as he stated in his introduction. His primary reliance in that was on the book of the scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha: 'Tashih al-Quduri'. Al-Maidani stated in the introduction of al-Lubab that he included what the scholar Qasim had collected of the imams' choices for the preponderant and correct. This work of Qasim is a great and magnificent work, serving the madhhab excellently. This inclusion by al-Maidani of Tashih al-Quduri varies in extent from issue to issue: sometimes he quotes its text verbatim, often he summarizes it, and rarely he omits it despite its importance for that issue. On this occasion I note that I have tried hard to complete al-Maidani's path in explaining the relied-upon mufta bihi in the madhhab where he missed it, or where there is a correction or a difference in tashih, from 'Tashih al-Quduri' and from other madhhab works concerned with explaining this aspect. He also relied on the book 'al-Hidayah' in explaining the mufta bihi, and on what his teacher the scholar Ibn Abidin recorded in his commentary on al-Durr al-Mukhtar. Al-Maidani then presented summaries of what he mentioned. Likewise, he relied on the book 'al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah' and on the book...
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is from the introductory study of the book al-Lubab, explaining the methodology of its author, al-Maidani, in selecting the strongest and most authoritative rulings of the Hanafi madhhab. The text begins by discussing the complexity of istidlal (legal reasoning), noting that each imam has his own principles of deduction, and that the science of hadith authentication is separate. The author then criticizes those who write comparative fiqh works with incomplete evidence and hasty judgments. The main focus is on al-Maidani's approach in al-Lubab: he sought to mention the most sound and strongest positions when there was ikhtilaf among the Hanafi imams, relying primarily on 'Tashih al-Quduri' by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, which compiles the preponderant choices of the imams. Al-Maidani also used 'al-Hidayah' and the marginalia of Ibn Abidin on al-Durr al-Mukhtar. The commentator (the author of this study) states that he himself attempted to fill in gaps or correct what was missing. This lesson is methodological front matter, not a specific fiqh ruling.

Key Terms
تصحيح القدوري (Tashih al-Quduri): A work by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha that identifies the strongest (mufta bihi) positions in al-Quduri's Mukhtasar within the Hanafi madhhab.
المعتمد المختار للفتوى (al-mu'tamad al-mukhtar lil-fatwa): The relied-upon, chosen position for issuing fatwas, i.e., the authoritative view within the madhhab that should be followed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Which book did al-Maidani primarily rely on for selecting the mufta bihi positions in al-Lubab?
A) Al-Hidayah
B) Tashih al-Quduri
C) Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah
D) Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi

Key Takeaway
Al-Maidani's method in al-Lubab was to systematically select the strongest Hanafi positions using Tashih al-Quduri as the primary arbiter of ikhtilaf.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Methodology of al-Lubab and Reliance on Tashih al-Quduri
Explains al-Maydani's sources and method for tarjih in al-Lubab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the primary and secondary sources that al-Maydani relied on for determining the mu'tamad (relied-upon) positions in al-Lubab, and explain the role of tarjih in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Al-Maydani's al-Lubab primarily relies on Tashih al-Quduri to select the strongest Hanafi rulings for fatwa.

The methodology of a classical Hanafi text is not arbitrary; it reflects a careful selection process rooted in authoritative sources. This passage from the study of al-Lubab reveals how al-Maydani chose the strongest opinions for fatwa, drawing primarily on Tashih al-Quduri by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha. Understanding this foundation helps the student appreciate why certain rulings are preferred and how tarjih operates within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary source
Locate the phrase indicating al-Maydani's first reliance. The passage states: 'wa kana i'timaduhu al-awwal fi dhalika 'ala kitab... Tashih al-Quduri.'
Tashih al-Quduri is a work that collects and corrects preferred opinions from Hanafi imams.
2
Describe usage patterns
The passage mentions three ways al-Maydani uses Tashih al-Quduri: quoting verbatim, summarizing, and rarely omitting. Note this variation.
This shows flexibility while maintaining core reliance.
3
List secondary sources
Identify other authorities mentioned: al-Hidayah, Ibn Abidin's Hashiyah, al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, and Durar al-Hukkam.
These supplement the primary source.
4
Understand the tarjih complexity
The passage discusses various methodologies for preferring opinions among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, etc. Some prefer the Imam always, others weigh evidence or circumstances.
This underscores the importance of Tashih al-Quduri as a stabilizing reference.
5
Note indirect transmission
Corrections from al-Nasafi, Burhan al-Shari'ah, and Sadr al-Shari'ah come indirectly via Tashih al-Quduri.
This highlights the intermediary role of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب
۱۰ ـ اهتم صاحب اللباب كثيراً، بل تحرى ذِكْرَ الأصح والأقوى، والمعتمد المختار للفتوى، وذلك حال وجود خلاف بين أئمة المذهب في المسائل المذكورة، كما صرح بذلك في مقدمته. وكان اعتماده الأول في ذلك على كتاب العلامة قاسم بن قطلوبغا: «تصحيح القدوري»، وقد صرّح الميداني في مقدمة اللبــاب بضم ما جَمَعَه العلامة قاسم من اختيارات الأئمة لمـا هـو الراجح والصحيح. وهذا العمل الذي قام به العلامة قاسم عمل عظيم جليل، خَدَم به المذهب خدمة جليلة.
وهذا الضم والاحتواء من الميداني لتصحيح القدوري، يختلف قدره من مسألة لأخرى، فأحياناً يورد الميداني نصه كما هو، وأحياناً كثيرة يختصره، وفي أحيان قليلة يترك ذكره، مع كونه مهماً في تلـك المسألة.
وبهذه المناسبة أشير إلى أني قد حاولت جاهداً إتمام مسيرة الميداني في بيان المعتمد المفتى به في المذهب فيما فاته، أو فيما فيه استدراك، أو اختلاف تصحيح، وذلك من «تصحيح القدوري»، ومن غيره من كتب المذهب المهتمة ببيان هذا الجانب.
كما اعتمد الميداني أيضاً على كتاب «الهداية» في بيان المفتى به، وعلى ما سجله شيخه العلامة ابن عابدين في حاشيته علـى الـدر المختار، فيأتي الميداني بخلاصات مما ذكره.
وهكذا كان يعتمد على كتاب «الجوهرة النيرة»، وعلى كتاب درر الحكام شرح غرر الأحكام لمنلا خسرو، وغيرهـا مـن كتـب المذهب.
مختلفةٌ
وأما ما في اللباب من نَقل تصحيحات وترجيحات عن النسفي وبرهان الشريعة وصدر الشريعة فهي بالواسطة عن طريق تصحيح القدوري للعلامة قاسم. وبهذه المناسبة، أنبه هنا إلى أن مسألة بيان الراجح في المذهب، ومعرفة المفتى به والمعتمد حال اختلاف أقوال أئمة المذهب، مسألة شائكة عريضةٌ مهمة، وفيها وجهات نظر لأئمة المذهب من المتقدمين والمتأخرين، متباينة تأصيلاً وتفريعاً. فمنهم من يجعل قول الإمام هو المقدم دائماً، ومنهم من يرجح قول أحد أصحابه وخاصة الصاحبين، وهؤلاء منهم من يجعل سبب الترجيح قوة الدليل، وبذا يكون المرجح قد نصب نفسه حكماً بينهم، أو يكون الترجيح للتيسير ، أو لاختلاف الزمان والمكان، أو اتباعاً لترجيح مرجح من أئمة المذهب...، وهكذا يحتاج الأمر إلى كتابة مفردة دقيقة محررة، مع كل ما كتب فيها.
وكذلك مسألة أخرى مهمة تتصل بها وهي: كيف دخلت أقوال الأصحاب أبي يوسف ومحمد وزفر في المذهب، ونُسبت إليه، وسمي الجميع مذهب أبي حنيفة؟
أسأل الله تعالى أن ييسر لي إتمام الكتابة في بيان ذلك، وتحريره وتنقيحه، مع السداد والتوفيق.
١١- صرح الشارح الميداني في مقدمـة اللباب أنـه جَمَعَ فيـه
Chapter Two: Study of al-Lubab
10 — The author of al-Lubab paid great attention, rather he sought to mention the most sound (asahh) and strongest (aqwa), and the relied-upon and chosen for fatwa, when there was a difference among the imams of the madhhab in the mentioned issues, as he stated in his introduction. His primary reliance in that was on the book of the scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha: 'Tashih al-Quduri'. Al-Maydani stated in the introduction of al-Lubab that he included what the scholar Qasim had collected of the imams' selections for what is preponderant (rajih) and correct. This work done by the scholar Qasim is a great and noble work, by which he rendered a great service to the madhhab.
This inclusion and incorporation by al-Maydani of Tashih al-Quduri varies in extent from one issue to another: sometimes he quotes its text as is, often he summarizes it, and in rare cases he leaves it out despite its importance in that issue.
On this occasion, I point out that I have striven hard to complete al-Maydani's path in clarifying the relied-upon (mu'tamad) and fatwa-given (mufta bihi) in the madhhab in what he omitted, or where there is correction or difference in verification, from 'Tashih al-Quduri' and from other books of the madhhab concerned with clarifying this aspect.
Al-Maydani also relied on the book 'al-Hidayah' in clarifying the mufta bihi, and on what his teacher the scholar Ibn Abidin recorded in his Hashiyah on al-Durr al-Mukhtar; al-Maydani brings summaries of what he mentioned.
Thus he also relied on the book 'al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah', and on the book 'Durar al-Hukkam Sharh Ghurar al-Ahkam' by Mulla Khosrow, and other books of the madhhab.
And as for what is in al-Lubab of transmitted corrections and preferences (tashihāt and tarjīhāt) from al-Nasafi, Burhan al-Shari'ah, and Sadr al-Shari'ah, they are indirectly through Tashih al-Quduri by the scholar Qasim. On this occasion, I draw attention that the issue of clarifying the preponderant (rajih) in the madhhab, and knowing the mufta bihi and relied-upon when there are differences among the imams of the madhhab, is a thorny, broad, important issue. There are viewpoints of the imams of the madhhab from the earlier and later scholars, diverse in principles and branches. Some always give precedence to the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa), others prefer the statement of one of his companions (sahibayn). Among these, some make the cause of preference the strength of evidence, so that the preferrer has appointed himself as judge between them; or the preference is for facilitation, or due to difference of time and place, or following the preference of a preferrer among the imams of the madhhab... etc. Thus the matter requires a precise, refined independent writing, with all that has been written about it.
And likewise another important issue connected to it: How did the statements of the companions Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar enter the madhhab and become attributed to it, and all be called the madhhab of Abu Hanifah?
I ask Allah Almighty to facilitate for me the completion of writing about that, its editing and refinement, with correctness and success.
11 — The commentator al-Maydani stated in the introduction of al-Lubab that he collected in it...
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is a study of the methodology of the book 'al-Lubab' by al-Maydani. It explains the author's primary sources for determining the relied-upon (mu'tamad) and fatwa-worthy (mufta bihi) positions within the Hanafi school. The key source is 'Tashih al-Quduri' by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, which compiled the preferred rulings from the early imams. Al-Maydani sometimes quotes it verbatim, often summarizes it, and rarely omits it. The passage also mentions other sources: 'al-Hidayah', Ibn Abidin's 'Hashiyah', 'al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah', and 'Durar al-Hukkam'. It highlights the complexity of tarjih (preferring one opinion over another) within the Hanafi madhhab, noting differing methodologies among scholars—some always prioritize Abu Hanifa's view, while others consider the strength of evidence or practical convenience. The passage ends with a reflection on how the opinions of Abu Hanifa's disciples became integrated into the madhhab. This serves as an important orientation for the student: the rulings in 'al-Lubab' are not arbitrary but based on a careful selection process drawing from authoritative sources.

Key Terms
تصحيح القدوري (Tashih al-Quduri): A book by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha that corrects and prefers one opinion over another from the Hanafi imams on issues in al-Quduri's matn.
المعتمد المختار للفتوى (al-mu'tamad al-mukhtar lil-fatwa): The relied-upon and chosen position that is to be given as a fatwa.
الترجيح (al-tarjih): The process of preferring one scholarly opinion over another based on strength of evidence or other criteria.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Tashih al-Quduri by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha
C) Hashiyah by Ibn Abidin
D) Durar al-Hukkam by Mulla Khosrow

Key Takeaway
Al-Maydani's al-Lubab carefully selects relied-upon Hanafi rulings primarily from Tashih al-Quduri, supplemented by other authoritative works, reflecting the complex process of tarjih in the school.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Sources and Methodology of Al-Lubab: The Tarjih Issue
This passage critiques the sources and methodology of Al-Lubab, highlighting the complexity of tarjih in the Hanafi school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the primary source of Al-Lubab and explain why the issue of tarjih is complex in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Tarjih in the Hanafi school is not monolithic; it involves weighing statements of Imam and his companions based on evidence and context.

This lesson explores the background of Al-Lubab, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Maydani. We examine the author's heavy reliance on Al-Hidayah and the intricate issue of tarjih within the Hanafi school, where preferences among Abu Hanifa and his disciples are debated. Understanding these sources and preferences is crucial for proper fiqh application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main source of Al-Lubab
Read the passage to find which work al-Maydani relied on most. Note that it is Al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani, which itself combines Mukhtasar al-Quduri and Al-Jami' al-Saghir.
Al-Maydani quotes Al-Hidayah explicitly or implicitly in many places.
2
Understand the chain of transmission
The passage mentions that corrections and preferences from al-Nasafi, Burhan al-Shari'ah, etc., reach Al-Lubab indirectly via 'Allamah Qasim's correction of al-Quduri. Trace this indirect attribution.
Such indirect transmission can affect the reliability of the transmitted view.
3
Recognize the complexity of tarjih
The author notes that scholars differ on whether to always prefer Abu Hanifa's opinion or that of his companions. Reasons for preferring a companion's view include strength of evidence, convenience, or time/place considerations.
Tarjih is not a simple rule but depends on multiple factors.
4
Note the omission of faraid in Al-Hidayah
Al-Marghinani omitted the book of inheritance from Al-Hidayah because it was not in Al-Jami' al-Saghir, even though it is in Mukhtasar al-Quduri. This omission affects those relying solely on Al-Hidayah.
Students of fiqh must be aware of such gaps when using Al-Hidayah.
5
Assess the implications for fiqh study
Consider how the reliance on summarized texts and indirect transmission can lead to errors, as seen in the purification of khuff. This highlights the need for critical engagement with sources.
Al-Maydani's summarizations sometimes caused confusion or error.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب
درر الحكام شرح غرر الأحكام لمنلا خسرو، وغيرهـا مـن كتـب المذهب.
مختلفــةٌ
وأما ما في اللباب من نَقل تصحيحات وترجيحات عن النسفي وبرهان الشريعة وصدر الشريعة فهي بالواسطة عن طريق تصحيح القدوري للعلامة قاسم. وبهذه المناسبة، أنبه هنا إلى أن مسألة بيان الراجح في المذهب، ومعرفة المفتى به والمعتمد حال اختلاف أقوال أئمة المذهب، مسألة شائكة عريضةٌ مهمة، وفيها وجهات نظر لأئمة المذهب من المتقدمين والمتأخرين، متباينة تأصيلاً وتفريعاً. فمنهم من يجعل قول الإمام هو المقدم دائماً، ومنهم من يرجح قول أحد أصحابه وخاصة الصاحبين، وهؤلاء منهم من يجعل سبب الترجيح قوة الدليل، وبذا يكون المرجح قد نصب نفسه حكماً بينهم، أو يكون الترجيح للتيسير ، أو لاختلاف الزمان والمكان، أو اتباعاً لترجيح مرجح من أئمة المذهب...، وهكذا يحتاج الأمر إلى كتابة مفردة دقيقة محررة، مع كل ما كتب فيها.
وكذلك مسألة أخرى مهمة تتصل بها وهي: كيف دخلت أقوال الأصحاب أبي يوسف ومحمد وزفر في المذهب، ونُسبت إليه، وسمي الجميع مذهب أبي حنيفة؟
أسأل الله تعالى أن ييسر لي إتمام الكتابة في بيان ذلك، وتحريره وتنقيحه، مع السداد والتوفيق.
١١- صرح الشارح الميداني في مقدمـة اللباب أنـه جَمَعَ فيـه عبارات تكون كالشرح على مختصر القدوري مع زيادات مستحسنة يضيفها من عنده.
وكان من منهجه رحمه الله في ذلك عزو ما نقله لقائله، إلا أحياناً قليلة، وأحياناً يكون العزو بالواسطة، وليس بشكل مباشر.
١٢ ـ من أهم المصادر التي اعتمدها الميداني في اللباب لشرح عبارة القدوري : كتاب «الهداية للمرغيناني، بتصريح في الأغلب. وبغير تصريح في مواضع كثيرة. وقد أكثر الميداني من النقل عن الهداية جداً، والسبب في ذلك أن كتاب الهداية من أهم الكتب المعتمدة عند الحنفية، وقد جمع صاحب الهداية في كتابه: بداية المبتدي بين مختصر القدوري، والجامع الصغير للإمام محمد بن الحسن الشيباني، ثم شرح ذلك في الهداية، ولذا يُعتبر كتاب الهداية من شروح القدوري.
وقد اعتمد صاحب الهداية ترتيب الجامع الصغير، دون ترتيب القدوري، كما أن المرغيناني أسقط من بداية المبتدي والهداية كتـاب الفرائض والمواريث، لعدم وجوده في الجامع الصغير، مع أنـه موجود في مختصر القدوري.
وهذه النقول عن الهداية أحياناً يوردها الميداني بالنص، وأحياناً كثيرة جداً يختصرها ليفيد القارئ بالمراد، لكـن هـذا الاختصار كان يسبب في بعض الأحيان إشكالاً، أو صعوبة في فهم النص، وأحياناً قليلة جداً يجعل خللاً في النص، كما حصل في مسألة تطهير الخُف إذا أصابته نجاسة ومسائل أخرى، مما سيراه
Chapter Two: Study of Al-Lubab
Durar al-Hukkam Sharh Ghurar al-Ahkam by Mulla Khusraw, and other books of the school.
Various
As for what is in Al-Lubab of transmitted corrections and preferences from al-Nasafi, Burhan al-Shari'ah, and Sadr al-Shari'ah, it is indirectly via the correction of Al-Quduri by 'Allamah Qasim. On this occasion, I draw attention here to the fact that the issue of clarifying the preferred view in the school, and knowing the fatwa-issuing and relied-upon position when there is disagreement among the statements of the imams of the school, is a complex, broad, and important matter. There are differing viewpoints among the imams of the school, both early and later, diverging in principles and application. Some of them always give precedence to the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa), while others prefer the statement of one of his companions, especially the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Among these, some make the reason for preference the strength of evidence, and thus the one who gives preference has appointed himself as judge among them, or the preference is for convenience, or due to differences of time and place, or following the preference of a preponderator among the imams of the school... Thus, the matter requires a precise and refined independent writing, along with everything written on it.
And another important matter connected to it is: how did the statements of the companions Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar enter the school, and become attributed to it, and all be called the school of Abu Hanifa?
I ask Allah Almighty to facilitate for me the completion of writing about that, and its revision and correction, with correctness and success.
11. The commentator al-Maydani stated in his introduction to Al-Lubab that he compiled in it expressions that serve as a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, with beneficial additions he added from himself.
His methodology, may Allah have mercy on him, in that was to attribute what he transmitted to its original author, except rarely, and sometimes the attribution was indirect, not direct.
12. One of the most important sources that al-Maydani relied upon in Al-Lubab to explain the text of al-Quduri is the book 'Al-Hidayah' by al-Marghinani, explicitly in most cases, and implicitly in many places. Al-Maydani frequently transmitted from Al-Hidayah very often, and the reason is that Al-Hidayah is one of the most important authoritative books among the Hanafis. The author of Al-Hidayah compiled in his book 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi' between Mukhtasar al-Quduri and Al-Jami' al-Saghir by Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, then explained that in Al-Hidayah. Thus, Al-Hidayah is considered one of the commentaries on Al-Quduri.
The author of Al-Hidayah adopted the arrangement of Al-Jami' al-Saghir, not the arrangement of Al-Quduri. Moreover, al-Marghinani omitted from Bidayat al-Mubtadi and Al-Hidayah the book of inheritance (fara'id and mawarith), because it is not in Al-Jami' al-Saghir, even though it is present in Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
Al-Maydani sometimes quotes these transmissions from Al-Hidayah verbatim, and very often he summarizes them to benefit the reader with the intended meaning, but this summarization sometimes caused confusion or difficulty in understanding the text, and very rarely it caused an error in the text, as happened in the issue of purifying the khuff (leather sock) when it is hit by impurity, and other issues, as will be seen.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is a study of Al-Lubab, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Maydani. The author begins by noting that corrections and preferences from certain scholars are transmitted indirectly via Qasim's correction of al-Quduri. He then raises a critical point: determining the preferred ruling within the Hanafi school is a complex matter. Scholars differ on whether to give precedence to Abu Hanifa, his two companions, or others. Some prioritize strength of evidence, others convenience or time/place considerations. The author also questions how the opinions of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar became incorporated into the school. Al-Maydani's methodology is to compile commentary with additions, attributing sources mostly directly but sometimes indirectly. The main source is Al-Hidayah, which itself is a commentary on Al-Quduri and Al-Jami' al-Saghir. However, al-Marghinani omitted the book of inheritance from Al-Hidayah, even though it is in Al-Quduri. Al-Maydani often summarizes Al-Hidayah, which sometimes leads to obscurity or error, as exemplified by the purification of the khuff.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjih): The process of preferring one legal ruling over another within the Hanafi school, often based on strength of evidence or other criteria.
المفتى به (al-mufta bihi): The operative ruling that is to be issued as a fatwa, the relied-upon position in the school.
الهداية (Al-Hidayah): The famous Hanafi fiqh work by al-Marghinani, combining Mukhtasar al-Quduri and Al-Jami' al-Saghir, and a primary source for al-Maydani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary source that al-Maydani relied upon in Al-Lubab?
A) Mukhtasar al-Quduri
B) Al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani
C) Al-Jami' al-Saghir
D) Durar al-Hukkam

Key Takeaway
Al-Lubab is heavily reliant on Al-Hidayah, and the Hanafi school's tarjih process requires careful consideration of multiple factors, not a simple preference for Abu Hanifa.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
Al-Maydani's Sources and Methodology in Al-Lubab
Front-matter description of al-Maydani's methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sources, methodology, and scope of al-Maydani's commentary Al-Lubab, and identify the key texts in the Hanafi tradition that it draws upon.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab is a Hanafi-only commentary that heavily relies on Al-Hidayah, itself a fusion of Quduri and Shaybani's works.

Al-Lubab is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, but it is not just any commentary. Al-Maydani structured it as a blend of his own explanations and extensive quotations from earlier authoritative works, primarily Al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani and Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah by al-Haddadi. Understanding his methodology—his attribution habits, his abbreviation tendencies, and his exclusive focus on the Hanafi school—helps you read Al-Lubab with the right expectations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core texts in the chain
Recognize that Al-Lubab is a sharh of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, which itself is a foundational text. Al-Quduri was combined with Al-Jami' al-Saghir in Al-Marghinani's Bidayat al-Mubtadi, then commented upon in Al-Hidayah. So Al-Hidayah is a key intermediary.
2
Trace al-Maydani's use of Al-Hidayah
He quotes it explicitly or implicitly, often abbreviating. This abbreviation can cause confusion or errors. Why does he rely on Al-Hidayah so heavily? Because it is a central Hanafi authority that synthesizes two major sources.
3
Note the drop of Fara'id
Al-Marghinani omitted the book of inheritance from his works because it was not in Al-Jami' al-Saghir, even though it is in al-Quduri. This explains why Al-Lubab also lacks a full treatment of fara'id.
4
Identify the second major source: Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah
This is another commentary on al-Quduri by al-Haddadi, also frequently used, sometimes with explicit attribution.
5
Understand the scope and limitations
Al-Lubab is exclusively Hanafi; it does not aim to compare madhhabs except rarely. Al-Maydani occasionally notes variant readings in manuscripts of al-Quduri but not consistently.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب
عبارات تكون كالشرح على مختصر القدوري مع زيادات مستحسنة يضيفها من عنده.
وكان من منهجه رحمه الله في ذلك عزو ما نقله لقائله، إلا أحياناً قليلة، وأحياناً يكون العزو بالواسطة، وليس بشكل مباشر.
١٢ ـ من أهم المصادر التي اعتمدها الميداني في اللباب لشرح عبارة القدوري : كتاب «الهداية للمرغيناني، بتصريح في الأغلب. وبغير تصريح في مواضع كثيرة. وقد أكثر الميداني من النقل عن الهداية جداً، والسبب في ذلك أن كتاب الهداية من أهم الكتب المعتمدة عند الحنفية، وقد جمع صاحب الهداية في كتابه: بداية المبتدي بين مختصر القدوري، والجامع الصغير للإمام محمد بن الحسن الشيباني، ثم شرح ذلك في الهداية، ولذا يُعتبر كتاب الهداية من شروح القدوري.

وهذه النقول عن الهداية أحياناً يوردها الميداني بالنص، وأحياناً كثيرة جداً يختصرها ليفيد القارئ بالمراد، لكـن هـذا الاختصار كان يسبب في بعض الأحيان إشكالاً، أو صعوبة في فهم النص، وأحياناً قليلة جداً يجعل خللاً في النص، كما حصل في مسألة تطهير الخُف إذا أصابته نجاسة ومسائل أخرى، مما سيراه القارىء في موضعه.
وأيضاً فقد أكثر الميداني النقل عن «الجوهرة النيرة» شرح القدوري، للحدادي، بتصريح في العزو إليه، وبدون تصريح
١٣ ـ كتاب اللباب خاص بذكر المذهب الحنفي دون غيره، ولا يتعرض لذكر الفقه المقارن بين المذاهب الأربعة المشتهرة، لكن الميداني في مواطن قليلة معدودة يذكر خلاف بقية المذاهب الأربعة، أدلة لطيفة بدون توسع مثل مسألة لقطة الأنعام من البقر والإبل، في كتاب اللقطة.
وأحياناً يكون الخلاف مذكوراً أصلاً في مختصر القدوري، وليس ضمن المذاهب الأربعة فحسب، بل بأوسع، وهـو نـادر قليل، مثل مسألة توريث الخنثى، حيث ذكر القدوري أن قول الصاحبين هو قول الإمام الشعبي
١٤ـ بالنسبة لبيان ما هو واقع من اختلاف في نسخ القدوري، فقد كان من عمل الشارح الميداني ومنهجه أنه يذكر أحياناً مـا وقـع له من خلاف بين النسخ ، ثم يبين أولى النسخ بالصواب والصحة، وليس هذا باطراد، فنُسَخُ القدوري فيها اختلافات كثيرة جداً، وعدد كبير من هذه المغايرات جوهري، ولا يشير إلى كلها، ومسألة اختلاف نسخ القدوري مسألة مهمة، وقد أفردتها في فصل خاص، سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى.
Chapter Two: Study of Al-Lubab. Passages that serve as commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri with beneficial additions that he adds from himself. His methodology, may Allah have mercy on him, was to attribute what he transmitted to its speaker, except occasionally, and sometimes the attribution was indirect, not directly. 12 - Among the most important sources that al-Maydani relied on in Al-Lubab to explain the statement of al-Quduri: the book 'Al-Hidayah' by al-Marghinani, explicitly in most cases, and without explicit mention in many places. Al-Maydani very frequently transmitted from Al-Hidayah, and the reason is that Al-Hidayah is among the most important authoritative books for the Hanafis. The author of Al-Hidayah in his book collected in Bidayat al-Mubtadi between Mukhtasar al-Quduri and Al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, then he explained that in Al-Hidayah, and therefore Al-Hidayah is considered one of the commentaries on al-Quduri. The author of Al-Hidayah adopted the arrangement of Al-Jami' al-Saghir, not the arrangement of al-Quduri. Also, al-Marghinani dropped from Bidayat al-Mubtadi and Al-Hidayah the book of Fara'id and Inheritance, because it was not present in Al-Jami' al-Saghir, even though it is present in Mukhtasar al-Quduri. These transmissions from Al-Hidayah are sometimes quoted by al-Maydani verbatim, and very often he abbreviates them to benefit the reader with the intended meaning, but this abbreviation sometimes caused confusion or difficulty in understanding the text, and very rarely caused an error in the text, as happened in the issue of purifying the khuff when it is affected by impurity and other issues, as the reader will see in its place. Also, al-Maydani frequently transmitted from 'Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah,' the commentary on al-Quduri by al-Haddadi, with explicit attribution to it, and without explicit mention. 13 - The book Al-Lubab is specific to mentioning the Hanafi madhhab only, and does not address comparative fiqh among the four famous madhhabs, but al-Maydani in a few rare places mentions the disagreement of the rest of the four madhhabs, with fine proofs without expansion, such as the issue of lost cattle (cows and camels) in the book of Luqatah. Sometimes the disagreement is already mentioned in Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and not only within the four madhhabs, but more broadly, and that is rare, such as the issue of the inheritance of the hermaphrodite, where al-Quduri mentioned that the view of the two companions is the view of Imam al-Sha'bi. 14 - Regarding the clarification of what exists of differences in copies of al-Quduri, it was part of the commentator al-Maydani's practice and methodology that he sometimes mentions what occurred to him of differences between the copies, then he shows which copies are most correct and sound, and this is not consistent, for the copies of al-Quduri have very many differences, and a large number of these discrepancies are substantive, and he does not point out all of them. The issue of differences in copies of al-Quduri is an important issue, and I have devoted a separate chapter to it, coming later, God willing.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter introduction from the study of Al-Lubab, explaining the author's methodology. The text first states that al-Maydani's work consists of commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri with beneficial additions. His practice was to attribute statements to their original authors, though sometimes indirectly. The primary source he relied on is Al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani, often used explicitly but also implicitly. Al-Hidayah itself is a commentary that combines al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir, thus it is a key Hanafi reference. Notably, al-Marghinani omitted the book of Fara'id from his work because it was not in al-Jami' al-Saghir, even though it exists in al-Quduri. Al-Maydani sometimes quotes verbatim from Al-Hidayah and often abbreviates, but this can cause confusion or errors. Another major source is Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah by al-Haddadi. The passage also clarifies that Al-Lubab is exclusively Hanafi, rarely mentioning other madhhabs. When it does, it is usually brief, as in the example of lost cattle. In rare cases, the disagreement appears already in al-Quduri and is more extensive, such as the inheritance of a hermaphrodite. Finally, al-Maydani occasionally notes differences between manuscript copies of al-Quduri, though not consistently, and he promises a separate chapter on the topic.

Key Terms
الهداية (Al-Hidayah): A comprehensive Hanafi fiqh commentary by al-Marghinani, based on Bidayat al-Mubtadi which combines Mukhtasar al-Quduri and Al-Jami' al-Saghir.
الجوهرة النيرة (Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Abu Bakr al-Haddadi (d. 800 AH), widely used in Hanafi circles.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A seminal Hanafi fiqh manual by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), considered a core text for Hanafi jurisprudence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah
B) Al-Hidayah
C) Bidayat al-Mubtadi
D) Al-Jami' al-Saghir

Key Takeaway
Al-Lubab is a Hanafi-focused commentary on al-Quduri, deeply indebted to Al-Hidayah and Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, and its understanding requires awareness of its textual sources and the author's methodological choices.
