Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Features and Methodology of al-Lubab
Describing the characteristics and methodology of al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key features of al-Lubab and explain al-Maydani's methodology in quoting sources and handling textual variants.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab expands al-Quduri's 12,000 issues to 50,000, focusing on the mufta bihi and introducing Hanafi works.

This passage from al-Lubab's introduction gives us insight into how the author, al-Maydani, approached his commentary. It highlights his reliance on earlier works like al-Jawharat al-Nira, his focus on the Hanafi school, and his attention to textual variants. Understanding these features helps us appreciate the value of al-Lubab as a teaching tool.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sources cited by al-Maydani
Scan the passage for explicit references to other works. Note that al-Maydani frequently quotes from al-Jawharat al-Nira and also incorporates Tashih al-Quduri.
This shows his method of building on earlier scholarship.
2
Determine the school scope of al-Lubab
Find statements about whether al-Lubab covers multiple madhahib or only the Hanafi school. The passage says it is 'special to mentioning the Hanafi school without others', with rare exceptions.
This focus makes it a reliable source for Hanafi rulings.
3
Analyze how al-Maydani deals with textual variants
Look for phrases about differences in copies of al-Quduri. Al-Maydani sometimes indicates which copy is more correct, but not consistently.
This is a methodological limitation he acknowledges.
4
Summarize the merits listed in the passage
Read the second section (Merits) and list the claimed advantages: precise, clear, medium size, many additional masail, focus on mufta bihi, and introduction to Hanafi books.
These merits explain why al-Lubab is a valued commentary.

القارىء في موضعه.
الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب
وأيضاً فقد أكثر الميداني النقل عن «الجوهرة النيرة» شرح القدوري، للحدادي، بتصريح في العزو إليه، وبدون تصريح.
١٣ ـ كتاب اللباب خاص بذكر المذهب الحنفي دون غيره، ولا يتعرض لذكر الفقه المقارن بين المذاهب الأربعة المشتهرة، لكن الميداني في مواطن قليلة معدودة يذكر خلاف بقية المذاهب الأربعة، أدلة لطيفة بدون توسع مثل مسألة لقطة الأنعام من البقر والإبل، مع في كتاب اللقطة.
وأحياناً يكون الخلاف مذكوراً أصلاً في مختصر القدوري، وليس ضمن المذاهب الأربعة فحسب، بل بأوسع، وهو نادر قليل، مثل مسألة توريث الخنثى، حيث ذكر القدوري أن قول الصاحبين هو قول الإمام الشعبي.
١٤ـ بالنسبة لبيان ما هو واقع من اختلاف في نسخ القدوري، فقد كان من عمل الشارح الميداني ومنهجه أنه يذكر أحياناً ما وقع له من خلاف بين النسخ، ثم يبين أولى النسخ بالصواب والصحة، وليس هذا باطراد، فنُسَخُ القدوري فيها اختلافات كثيرة جداً، وعدد كبير من هذه المغايرات جوهري، ولا يشير إلى كلها، ومسألة اختلاف نسخ القدوري مسألة مهمة، وقد أفردتها في فصل خاص، سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى.
المبحث الثاني
مزايا اللباب للميداني
- اللباب شرح لمتن متقدم متين معتبر في المذهب الحنفي معتمد كل الاعتماد عند الحنفية.
٢ـ إن شروح القدوري كثيرة جداً، لكن يمتاز اللباب بأنه شرح دقيق، واضح إلى حد كبير، متوسط في حجمه بالنسبة للشروح، وفيه من الفوائد ما لا تجده في غيره، وفيه فروع كثيرة جاءت زائدة على ما في القدوري، وإذا كان عدد مسائل القدوري يبلغ (١٢٠٠٠) مسألة، فإن عدد مسائل اللباب مع أصله يبلغ نحو خمسين ألف مسألة تقريباً. من مزايا كتاب اللباب أنه يهتم كثيراً بذكر الراجح المفتى به المعتمد في المذهب.
٤ إن تضمين الميداني لكتاب تصحيح القدوري» للعلامة قاسم، يوقف طالب العلم القارئ على أسماء كثير من كتب المذهب الحنفي، وأسماء مصنفيها، وبذلك تتكون لديه ذخيرة كبيرة، وحصيلة عظيمة في هذا الجانب المهم من المعلومات عن المذهب، مما يجعل القارئ متصلاً بأئمة مذهبه ومصنفاتهم، وتكون له بذلك صلة وصل ومعرفة بين الطالب والكتاب.
"The reader is in its place.
Chapter Two: Study about al-Lubab
And also, al-Maydani frequently quoted from 'al-Jawharat al-Nira' commentary on al-Quduri by al-Hadadi, sometimes explicitly attributing to it and sometimes without attribution.
13. The book al-Lubab is specifically about the Hanafi school and does not engage in comparative fiqh among the four well-known schools, but al-Maydani in a few rare places mentions the disagreement of the other three schools, with subtle proofs without expansion, such as the issue of lost livestock from cows and camels, along with in the book of lost property.
And sometimes the disagreement is originally mentioned in Mukhtasar al-Quduri, not only within the four schools but more broadly, and this is very rare, such as the issue of inheriting a hermaphrodite, where al-Quduri stated that the opinion of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is the opinion of Imam al-Sha'bi.
14. Regarding the explanation of what actually occurs of variation in the copies of al-Quduri, it was from the work of the commentator al-Maydani and his methodology that he sometimes mentions the variation he encountered among the copies, then shows which copy is more correct and authentic, but this is not consistent; the copies of al-Quduri have very many variations, and a large number of these differences are substantive, and he does not refer to all of them. The issue of variation in the copies of al-Quduri is an important matter, and I have devoted a separate chapter to it, coming soon if Allah wills.
The Second Section
Merits of al-Lubab by al-Maydani
- Al-Lubab is a commentary on a solid, respected, advanced text in the Hanafi school, fully relied upon by the Hanafis.
2. The commentaries on al-Quduri are very many, but al-Lubab is distinguished as a precise commentary, clear to a large extent, medium in size relative to the commentaries, and contains benefits that you do not find in others, and it contains many subsidiary issues added beyond those in al-Quduri. If the number of issues in al-Quduri reaches 12,000, then the number of issues in al-Lubab with its original is about fifty thousand issues approximately. Among the merits of the book al-Lubab is that it pays great attention to mentioning the preferred, fatwa-issued, relied-upon opinion in the school.
4. Indeed, al-Maydani's inclusion of the book 'Tashih al-Quduri' by 'Allamah Qasim acquaints the student reader with the names of many Hanafi school books and their authors, and thus he acquires a great store and a tremendous outcome in this important aspect of information about the school, making the reader connected to the imams of his school and their works, and thus he has a link and knowledge between the student and the book."
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is from the introductory chapter of al-Lubab, specifically the second chapter titled 'Study about al-Lubab' and the second section on 'Merits of al-Lubab by al-Maydani'. The author, al-Maydani, first notes that he frequently quotes from 'al-Jawharat al-Nira' (another commentary on al-Quduri by al-Hadadi), sometimes explicitly citing it and sometimes not. He then outlines key features of his book: (1) It is exclusively about the Hanafi school and does not normally engage in comparative fiqh, though in a very few places he briefly mentions the views of other schools, e.g., the issue of lost cattle in the book of luqatah. (2) Occasionally, disagreements mentioned are originally in al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and go beyond the four schools, like the case of a hermaphrodite's inheritance, where al-Quduri attributes the opinion of the two Sahibayn to Imam al-Sha'bi. (3) Al-Maydani sometimes notes textual variants between copies of al-Quduri, indicating which is more correct, but this is not consistent due to the many substantive variants. He promises a separate chapter on this. Then, in the merits section, he lists: al-Lubab is a commentary on a highly reliable Hanafi matn; it is precise, clear, medium-sized, and contains benefits not found elsewhere; it includes many additional mas'alah (sub-branches) beyond al-Quduri, bringing the total to about 50,000 issues vs. al-Quduri's 12,000; it focuses on the mufta bihi (relied-upon) rulings; and it incorporates Qasim's 'Tashih al-Quduri', which introduces students to many Hanafi works and authors, connecting them to the school's heritage.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): The title of al-Maydani's commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
القدوري (al-Quduri): Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri, the author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text.
الجوهرة النيرة (al-Jawharat al-Nira): A commentary on al-Quduri by Abu Bakr al-Hadadi (d. 800 AH), frequently quoted by al-Maydani.
تصحيح القدوري (Tashih al-Quduri): A work by al-Allamah Qasim (likely Ibn Qasim al-Hanafi) that corrects textual variants in al-Quduri.
الميداني (al-Maydani): Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (d. 1298 AH), the author of al-Lubab, a later Hanafi commentator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is a distinct feature of al-Lubab?
A) It covers all four madhahib in detail.
B) It mentions the preferred (mufta bihi) opinion.
C) It avoids citing other commentaries.
D) It has fewer issues than al-Quduri.

Key Takeaway
Al-Lubab is a comprehensive, mufta bihi-focused Hanafi commentary that exponentially expands al-Quduri while introducing students to the school's literature.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Merits of Al-Lubab: A Gateway to Hanafi Fiqh
Describing the merits and features of the Hanafi commentary Al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the distinctive features of Al-Lubab and explain why it is a relied-upon commentary in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab is a comprehensive, precise commentary that prioritizes the mufta bihi position and connects students to the Hanafi scholarly heritage.

This lesson explores the celebrated features of Al-Lubab, the commentary on Al-Quduri by Abdul-Ghani al-Maydani. You will learn how the book's comprehensiveness, focus on authoritative rulings, and meticulous source citation make it an indispensable tool for studying Hanafi fiqh at an intermediate level.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text and commentator
Recognize that Al-Lubab is a commentary on Al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi matn, and was written by Al-Maydani, a late Hanafi scholar.
Al-Quduri contains about 12,000 rulings.
2
Assess the scope of the work
Note the significant expansion: Al-Lubab together with its original text contains approximately 50,000 rulings, making it far more comprehensive than the base matn.
This includes additional furu' not found in Al-Quduri.
3
Recognize the focus on mufta bihi
Al-Lubab emphasizes the preferred (rajih), fatwa-issuing (mufta bihi), and relied-upon (mu'tamad) positions in the madhhab, which is crucial for practical application.
This helps students avoid rare or weak opinions.
4
Understand the inclusion of Tashih al-Quduri
Al-Maydani incorporates 'Allamah Qasim's Tashih al-Quduri, which introduces readers to many Hanafi books and authors, building a scholarly network.
This enhances the student's knowledge of the madhhab's literature.
5
Appreciate the methodology of source citation
The author consistently cites his sources, inspiring confidence and training readers in precise academic methodology, where a single letter change can alter a ruling.
This practice also reflects gratitude for knowledge, as quoted from Imam Abu 'Ubayd.

Chapter Two: A Study of Al-Lubab
151
Second Section
The Merits of Al-Lubab by Al-Maydani
- Al-Lubab is a commentary on a sound, firmly established early text (matn) in the Hanafi school, fully relied upon by the Hanafis.
2. The commentaries on Al-Quduri are very numerous, but Al-Lubab is distinguished by being a precise commentary, clear to a large extent, moderate in size relative to other commentaries, and it contains benefits that you will not find elsewhere. It includes many subsidiary branches (furu') that are additional to what is in Al-Quduri. Whereas the number of rulings in Al-Quduri is 12,000, the number of rulings in Al-Lubab together with its original text reaches approximately fifty thousand.
3. Among the merits of the book Al-Lubab is that it pays great attention to mentioning the preferred (al-rajih), mufta bih, and relied-upon (al-mu'tamad) positions in the madhhab.
4. Al-Maydani's inclusion of the book Tashih al-Quduri by 'Allamah Qasim [Ibn Qutlubugha] acquaints the student-reader with the names of many books of the Hanafi school and the names of their authors. Thus a great treasure and vast acquisition of information about the school is formed in this important aspect, making the reader connected to the imams of his school and their works, thereby establishing a link and knowledge between the student and the book.

152
Chapter Two: A Study of Al-Lubab
5. The book Al-Lubab is a commentary that is neither easy nor difficult, closer to clarity, and can be benefited from by students of the Hanafi school at all levels, each taking from it according to his situation and the extent of his knowledge.
6. Among the merits of the book Al-Lubab is the abundance of its diverse sources, from which Al-Maydani gleaned splendid great benefits and pearls of rulings, which you will not find collected elsewhere.
7. The author of Al-Lubab's attention to mentioning the source from which he transmits inspires great confidence in the reader regarding the information and rulings contained in Al-Lubab, especially knowing that its author is trustworthy and beyond trustworthy in what he transmits and relates, so much so that when the reader wishes to verify them, his heart is at ease.
Also, mentioning the source trains the reader in this blessed, precise, and sound academic methodology in what he transmits or relates of fiqh rulings, which require extreme precision in their transmission, for perhaps a change of a single letter changes the ruling. Also, part of gratitude for knowledge is that when you benefit from something and it is mentioned to you, you say: 'Such and such was hidden from me, and I had no knowledge of it until so-and-so informed me of it.' This is gratitude for knowledge. End quote from the words of Imam Abu 'Ubayd al-Qasim ibn Sallam, who died in 224 AH.
- Al-Lubab combined the majesty of the texts of the early scholars and their lights, and also [the rest is cut off].
(1) Al-Jami' li-Akhlaq al-Rawi wa Adab al-Sami' by al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, 2/154, 'Abu 'Ubayd al-Qasim ibn Sallam', by the writer of these letters, p. 59.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is an introductory study (المبحث الثاني) on the merits of the book Al-Lubab by Al-Maydani. It is not a fiqh ruling but rather a description of the work's features and scholarly value. The author begins by stating that Al-Lubab is a commentary on a foundational, reliable matn in the Hanafi school, fully depended upon. Then he notes the abundance of commentaries on Al-Quduri but singles out Al-Lubab for its precision, clarity, moderate size, and additional content. He highlights that while Al-Quduri has about 12,000 rulings, Al-Lubab together with its base text contains approximately 50,000 rulings, indicating its comprehensiveness. A key feature is its emphasis on the preferred and relied-upon positions (الراجح المعتمد المفتی به) in the madhhab, which is crucial for fatwa and practice. The inclusion of Tashih al-Quduri by 'Allamah Qasim (Qasim ibn Qutlubugha) serves to introduce readers to the names of many Hanafi works and authors, building a rich scholarly resource. The author describes the book as neither too easy nor too difficult, accessible to students at various levels. He praises the diversity of sources from which Al-Maydani drew, and the trustworthiness of the author, who carefully cites his sources. This practice not only ensures reliability but also trains the reader in rigorous methodology, emphasizing that a single letter change could alter a ruling. Finally, he quotes Imam Abu 'Ubayd on gratitude for knowledge. The passage concludes by stating that Al-Lubab combines the majesty of early texts with their lights, an incomplete sentence. Overall, this section serves to orient the reader to the value and scholarly credibility of the commentary Al-Lubab.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubāb): A commentary on Al-Quduri by Abdul-Ghani al-Maydani, known for its precision and reliance on Hanafi madhhab positions.
القدوري (al-Qudūrī): The matn (text) by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri, a foundational work in Hanafi fiqh containing about 12,000 rulings.
الميداني (al-Maydānī): Abdul-Ghani al-Maydani (d. 1298 AH), the author of al-Lubab and other Hanafi works.
الراجح المفتی به المعتمد (al-rājiḥ al-muftā bihi al-muʿtamad): The preferred (راجح) position that is issued as fatwa (مفتی به) and relied upon (معتمد) in the madhhab.
تصحيح القدوري (Taṣḥīḥ al-Qudūrī): A work by 'Allamah Qasim (Qasim ibn Qutlubugha) that corrects and annotates Al-Quduri. Al-Maydani includes it in his commentary.
المذهب الحنفي (al-madhhab al-ḥanafī): The Hanafi school of Islamic law, founded by Abu Hanifa and followed by Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and later scholars.

D) 5,000

Key Takeaway
Al-Lubab is a comprehensive Hanafi commentary that prioritizes the mufta bihi position and provides a rich bibliographic resource through its inclusion of Tashih al-Quduri.

Merits and Features of Al-Lubab
Describing the book al-Lubab's sources, clarity, and acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state at least three merits of Al-Lubab and explain why its source citation practice is important in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Al-Lubab is a trusted Hanafi commentary that bridges early and later scholars with clear source attribution.

This passage from the introduction of Al-Lubab outlines why the commentary is valuable for students at all levels. It emphasizes the book's diverse sources, meticulous citation, and its role in connecting the classical and later Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the passage
The passage is a preface describing the book’s features. Understand that it aims to convince the reader of the book’s reliability and usefulness.
2
List the merits of Al-Lubab
Go through the passage and extract each merit: clarity, diverse sources, citation of sources, combination of early and later scholarship, and scholarly acceptance.
Count at least four distinct merits.
3
Analyze the citation methodology
Note the author's care in mentioning sources and the quote from Imam Abu Ubayd about gratitude for knowledge. Reflect on why this builds trust.
The passage states that changing one letter can change a ruling, highlighting precision.
4
Understand the bridging role
Examine how Al-Lubab connects early texts (mutqadimun) and later contributions (mutakhkhirun) into a cohesive 'golden chain'.
Consider the metaphor of a golden chain and solid alloy.
5
Evaluate the acceptance of Al-Lubab
The passage notes that scholars received it well. Consider how this acceptance relates to the book's merits and its origin from Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب
ه كتاب اللباب شرح ليس بالسهل ولا بالصعب، وإلى الوضوح أقرب، ويمكن أن يستفيد منه طلاب المذهب الحنفي في كافــة مراحلهم، وكل منهم يأخذ منه على حسب حاله، وقدر علمه. ٦- من مزايا كتاب اللباب كثرة مصادره المتنوعة، التي التقط منها الميداني غُرَرَ الفوائد العظام، ودُرَرَ الأحكام، مما لا تجده مجموعاً في غير هذا المقام.

The second chapter: A study on al-Lubab. This book, al-Lubab, a commentary, is neither easy nor difficult, and is closer to clarity. Students of the Hanafi school can benefit from it at all their stages, and each takes from it according to his situation and knowledge. 6- Among the merits of the book al-Lubab is the abundance of its diverse sources, from which al-Maydani picked the great pearls of benefits and the gems of rulings, which you do not find collected elsewhere. 6- Indeed, the author of al-Lubab's care in mentioning the source from which he transmitted instills great confidence in the reader regarding the information and rulings contained in al-Lubab, along with the knowledge that its author is trustworthy and above trustworthiness in what he transmits and relates, such that if the reader wants to verify them to reassure his heart, he can. End quote from the words of Imam Abu Ubayd al-Qasim ibn Sallam, who died in 224 AH. - Al-Lubab combined the majesty of the texts of the early scholars and their lights, and the beauty of the jewels of the later scholars and their pearls, as it contained the choicest benefits and gathered many of the principles of the predecessors and the branches of the successors, until it became a continuous golden chain and a solid inseparable alloy, joining the grandchildren to the grandfathers and connecting the distant to the near. Among the merits of al-Lubab is that scholars received it with great good acceptance due to the many merits they found in it. Thus al-Lubab obtained a large share of what its original, Mukhtasar al-Quduri, obtained of blessing and wide circulation among the people of knowledge, and that is the bounty of Allah which He gives to whom He wills.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is from the introduction of Al-Lubab Sharh Al-Quduri, written by Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. It serves as a front matter describing the book's characteristics and merits. The author begins by stating that the commentary is neither too easy nor too difficult, but clear, making it suitable for students at all levels. He then lists several advantages: first, the book draws from a wide variety of sources, collecting valuable benefits and rulings not found together elsewhere. Second, the author (al-Maydani) is meticulous in citing his sources, which builds trust and trains readers in proper scholarly methodology, emphasizing that even a single letter change can alter a ruling. A quote from Imam Abu Ubayd al-Qasim ibn Sallam is included to highlight the importance of acknowledging who taught you something as a form of gratitude for knowledge. Third, the book bridges the works of early and later scholars, combining their principles and branches into a coherent whole. Finally, the author notes that scholars warmly received Al-Lubab, and it shares in the blessing and wide circulation of its base text, Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): The title of the commentary by al-Maydani on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, meaning 'the core' or 'pith'.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The celebrated Hanafi fiqh manual by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH/1037 CE), which serves as the base text for al-Lubab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is one of the main merits of al-Lubab mentioned in this passage?
A) It is easy enough for beginners only.
B) It combines sources from early and later scholars.
C) It is a collection of fatwas without references.
D) It only contains rulings from Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Key Takeaway
Al-Lubab is a well-sourced, clear commentary that unites early and later Hanafi scholarship, trusted for its accuracy and accepted widely.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
The Composition and Sources of al-Lubab: A Window into Hanafi Scholarly Practice
Historical analysis of al-Lubab's authoring timeline and source base.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the chronology of al-Lubab's authorship and identify the authoritative Hanafi sources that al-Maydani relied upon, and explain why provenance matters in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Know the book's chain: al-Lubab took nine years and drew from 19 key Hanafi works, anchoring it in the transmitted tradition.

Al-Maydani did not write in a vacuum. His Lubab is built on centuries of Hanafi scholarship. This lesson examines the time he spent and the books he used, giving us insight into the careful methodology of a Hanafi commentator. Understanding this helps you appreciate the authority of al-Lubab as a teaching text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's own statement
Look at what al-Maydani wrote in the zakat chapter about his progress. He mentions he was explaining it in 1261 AH.
This gives a fixed point during the writing process.
2
Reconcile the manuscript dates
The text notes two completion dates: 1266 and 1268. The commentator suggests a first draft in 1266 and a revised edition in 1268.
This shows the author's dedication to refinement.
3
Calculate the authorship period
Estimate the start year from the zakat point. If he reached zakat in 1261, he likely started earlier, around 1259. The final revision ends in 1268, giving about nine years.
The calculation is approximate but reveals a sustained effort.
4
Survey the source list
Note the 19 works cited, ranging from core matns like al-Kanz to major commentaries like al-Hidayah and fatwa collections.
These are all well-known references in the Hanafi school.
5
Assess the significance
Understand that using such authoritative sources strengthens al-Lubab's reliability. The list itself serves as a pedigree of the commentary.
A text's sources are part of its isnad in the broader sense.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن اللباب
المبحث الثالث
مدة تأليف اللباب
صرح المؤلف الميداني في آخر كتاب الزكاة أنه كان يشرحه سنة ١٢٦١هـ ، أي وله من العمر ٣٩ سنة، وقد انتهى منه مؤلفه سنة ١٢٦٦هـ.
وفي بعض مخطوطات اللباب أنه انتهى منه سنة ١٢٦٨هـ. قلت : ولعله انتهى منه أولاً سنة ١٢٦٦هـ، ثم أعاد النظـر فيـه لتنقيحه وتهذيبه، فكان الانتهاء منه تماماً في المرة الثانية محرراً منقحاً سنة ١٢٦٨هـ، والله أعلم.
وعلى هذا، إذا قدرنا أنه بدأ بتأليفه سنة ١٢٥٩هـ، حيث وصل إلى كتاب الزكاة سنة ١٢٦١هـ، وانتهـى مـنـه محـرراً منقحـاً سـنـة ١٢٦٨هـ، فتكون مدة تأليفه له حوالي تسع سنوات، والله أعلم.
المبحث الرابع
مصادر اللباب
جاء في الصفحة الأولى من طبعة اللباب سنة ١٢٧٥ العثمانية، التي طبعت في حياة المؤلف، جاء بيان ذكـر مـصـادر الميداني في اللباب بالعبارة التالية :
بيان ما في هذا الشرح اللطيف من المسائل المأخوذة من الكتب المعتبرة، التي صنّفها الفقهاء الأعلام رحمة الله عليهم، وعلى من ضبطها، وأجرى بمقتضاها الأحكام إلى يوم القيام:
۱ ـ كتاب الكنز، وبعض شروحه -۱۰ - الدرر والغرر لمنلا خسرو. ٢- الهداية، وبعض شروحها. ١١ - صدر الشريعة.
الجوهرة النيرة شرح القدوري. ١٢ ـ كتاب السراجية.
٤- تصحيح القدوري.

Chapter Two: Study of al-Lubab
Third Section: Duration of authorship of al-Lubab
The author, al-Maydani, stated at the end of the Book of Zakat that he was explaining it in the year 1261 AH, i.e., when he was 39 years old, and he completed his authorship in the year 1266 AH.
And in some manuscripts of al-Lubab, it says that he finished it in the year 1268 AH. I say: Perhaps he finished it first in 1266 AH, then reviewed it for revision and polishing, so the completion was fully revised in the second time in 1268 AH, and Allah knows best.
Based on this, if we estimate that he began authoring it in 1259 AH, having reached the Book of Zakat in 1261 AH, and finished it fully revised in 1268 AH, then the duration of its authorship would be about nine years, and Allah knows best.
Fourth Section: Sources of al-Lubab
On the first page of the Ottoman edition of al-Lubab of the year 1275, which was printed during the author's lifetime, a statement mentioning al-Maydani's sources in al-Lubab came with the following wording:
Statement of what this elegant commentary contains of issues taken from the reliable books composed by the eminent jurists, may Allah have mercy on them, and on those who recorded them and executed judgments according to them until the Day of Resurrection:
1. Kitab al-Kanz, and some of its commentaries.
2. al-Hidayah, and some of its commentaries.
3. al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, a commentary on al-Quduri.
4. Tashih al-Quduri.
5. Sharh al-Mujma'.
6. al-Mabsut.
7. al-Nahr al-Fa'iq.
8. al-Ikhtiyar, a commentary on al-Mukhtar.
9. al-Durar wa al-Ghurrar by Mulla Khusraw.
10. Sadr al-Shari'ah.
11. Kitab al-Sirajiyyah.
12. Jami' al-Fusulayn.
13. Fatawa Qadi Khan.
14. Sharh Fiqh Kaydani.
15. Qahistani.
16. al-Fatawa al-Khayriyyah.
17. al-Durr al-Mukhtar and some of its glosses.
18. Fatawa al-'Itabi.
19. al-Dhakhirah and others. End.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a historical study (دراسة) about the book *al-Lubab*, focusing on two aspects: the duration of its composition and the sources used by its author, Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. The author explicitly states in the chapter on zakat that he was working on it in 1261 AH (when he was 39), and the first completion was in 1266 AH. However, some manuscripts indicate a later date of 1268 AH. The commentator (the editor of the current edition) reconciles this by suggesting that al-Maydani finished a first draft in 1266 and then spent two years revising until 1268, making the total authorship period about nine years (1259-1268). The second part lists 19 sources, mostly authoritative Hanafi works, that al-Maydani relied upon. These include well-known works like *al-Kanz*, *al-Hidayah*, *al-Mabsut*, and *al-Ikhtiyar*, as well as fatwa collections and commentaries. This demonstrates the scholarly rigor and reliance on the established Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubab): The book being studied; a commentary (sharh) on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar by Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani.
الميداني (al-Maydani): The author of al-Lubab, a Hanafi jurist and commentator from the 13th century AH.
القدوري (al-Quduri): The author of the matn (Mukhtasar al-Quduri), a foundational text in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Lubab's nine-year composition and its reliance on 19 authoritative works confirm its place as a carefully crafted, tradition-rooted Hanafi commentary.
